Current Affairs Commentary

A Word for the National Lawyers' Community 14

— Yuan

The 7th National Lawyers Association Congress is being held in Shanghai, bringing together representatives from dozens of public organizations. The motions under discussion are numerous. The task of lawyers in the nation and society is to uphold justice, protect human rights, assist judicial organs, and consolidate the spirit of the rule of law. The gathering of this free profession has its own special significance. I would like to take this opportunity to say a word to the gentlemen of the lawyers' community.

Although the lawyer system in our country has been in place for several decades, the qualifications for lawyers in the late Qing Dynasty and early Republic of China were strictly screened. Recently, the restrictions have been relaxed, and the number of law school graduates applying for lawyer certificates has gradually increased. Coupled with the underdeveloped nature of various social undertakings, most of those with lawyer qualifications register and perform their duties in major cities, creating a sense of excess in the lawyer community. In fact, the use of lawyers is not limited to litigation cases. Non-litigation matters are many times more numerous than litigation cases. If more attention can be paid to this, the services that lawyers can provide to society will be even greater.

When the country is in a period of transition, not only do the common people lack the concept of abiding by the law, but even those in power may not be able to uphold the law like a deity. If the judiciary cannot demonstrate its independent spirit and instead caters to and complies with the powerful and foreign forces, it will forfeit its national integrity, which is extremely painful. Therefore, we rely on righteous people in the legal community to rise up and correct right and wrong in the world, clarify the true meaning of the law, redress grievances, and suppress evil. The hinge of the country's survival is in this.

This congress has dozens of motions, some suggesting to the authorities, some encouraging themselves, some seeking changes in procedures, and some planning to consolidate legal rights. All of these come from the hardships and sweetness of daily experience. The aim is that each of the motions should not merely increase the archives, but also manifest in actions and be deeply and clearly evident.

Since the gentlemen of the legal community are determined to serve society, the foundation of everything should be based on morality. Those who study the law should not fail to take morality as their essence. The social changes and machinations are endlessly resourceful and require accumulated experience to cope with. Too rigid will break, too soft will bend. Wise and upright behavior will be appropriate.

How many sages and philosophers in the legal community of Europe and America have risen to govern the country? Now our country will transition from tutelage to constitutionalism. People from the agricultural, industrial, and commercial sectors are not familiar with politics, and may not understand the law. If the representatives, in addition to performing their duties, examine the pain points of the people, study the gains and losses of the current politics, what legal aspects should be improved, and what social matters must be reformed, then the future of the country will truly depend on them.

New Brazilian Envoy to China, Mr. Leitão da Cunha, Presents Credentials, Lays Wreath at Mausoleum, Mr. Zhang Hosts a Banquet 15

Nanjing: The newly appointed Brazilian Envoy to China, Mr. Leitão da Cunha, visited Chairman Lin at the National Government at 11:00 AM on the 21st to present his credentials. At 10:40 AM, Mr. Mao Zhongfang, Director of the Bureau of Ceremonies of the National Government, and Mr. Liu Naifan, Section Chief, took the official and deputy limousines to the Envoy's residence at the Capital Hotel to welcome him. Mr. Leitão da Cunha, accompanied by Mr. Barboza, the Embassy Secretary, arrived at the National Government at 11:00 AM, accompanied by Mr. Mao and Mr. Liu. A platoon of guards was lined up along the driveway inside the gate of the National Government, commanded by senior officers. Also, a band played the Brazilian national anthem as the Envoy arrived. Receptionist Mr. Li Youchu of the Bureau of Ceremonies and Mr. Lin Tongshi of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs greeted the Envoy at the disembarkation point and led him to the reception room to rest. Then, the Director of the Bureau of Ceremonies entered to inform the Chairman, who came to the hall and stood in the center. Mr. Wei Huai, the Chief Secretary, led all the secretaries, and Mr. Lü Chao, the Chief Aide-de-Camp, led all the military personnel, lining up on both sides. Foreign Minister Zhang Qun and Mr. Duan Maolan, a translator from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, stood on the Chairman's right. Once the arrangements were complete, the Director of the Bureau of Ceremonies invited the Envoy to the audience. The Envoy entered the hall, performed the ceremony, and then began to deliver his remarks. After the translation was completed by the translator, the Envoy presented his credentials. The Chairman accepted them and handed them to the Foreign Minister. Then, the Chairman began to recite his response, and the translator recited the translated text. The Envoy stepped forward, and the Chairman shook his hand. The Chairman first asked about the health of the President of Brazil, and the translator conveyed the message. After a brief exchange, the Envoy introduced the Embassy staff, and the Chairman shook hands with them. The Envoy bid farewell, and the Director of the Bureau of Ceremonies led him out of the hall. After taking a photo with the Foreign Minister and the two Chiefs, they entered the reception room to rest and had some refreshments. The Envoy then bid farewell, and the personnel who had been sent to welcome him to the Embassy accompanied the Envoy and others in the original car back to the residence. The translated text of the Envoy's remarks and the full text of the Chairman's response are recorded below: Translated text of the Envoy's remarks: Your Excellency, Chairman: I have the honor to present to Your Excellency, the esteemed Chairman, the credentials from His Excellency, the President of my country, appointing me as the Envoy Extraordinary and Minister Plenipotentiary to reside in your country, as well as the letter of recall of the previous Envoy. The government of my country sincerely hopes to maintain the long-standing friendship and mutual trust between our two countries. I am deeply aware of the importance of this great mission and will follow the efforts of my predecessors to this end. I hope to receive your kind assistance and the assistance of your government so that I can fulfill my duties. The President of my country has ordered me to convey to Your Excellency, the esteemed Chairman, his sincere admiration and to wish the Republic of China prosperity. I also extend my admiration and respect, and humbly request your consideration. Full text of the Chairman's response: Your Excellency, Envoy: I am pleased to receive Your Excellency's credentials as the Envoy Extraordinary and Minister Plenipotentiary of Brazil to China, bestowed by His Excellency, the President of your country. I am delighted to hear that you have conveyed the cordial and friendly intentions. I am pleased that you will fulfill your duties in China as you wish. The long-standing friendship and trust between our two countries will become even closer. It is a great pleasure that your government has selected such a capable person. The Chinese government will assist you in completing your great mission. I sincerely wish your country prosperity and the President of your country good health. Please convey my regards and wish you a pleasant stay. (21st Central News Agency Dispatch)

Nanjing: Mr. Leitão da Cunha, accompanied by Secretary Mr. Barboza and Mr. Qu Chang of the Liaison Section of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, visited the Mausoleum at 3:00 PM on the 21st to pay their respects and lay a wreath. They returned to the city after the ceremony. At 4:00 PM, Mr. Leitão da Cunha and his wife, accompanied by Mr. Barboza and his wife, visited Foreign Minister Zhang and his wife at the Foreign Minister's residence. Mr. and Mrs. Zhang personally received them, and Mr. Duan Maolan and others were present to provide refreshments and translation. The conversation was very pleasant. Zhang also sent staff to present business cards in return in the afternoon. At 8:00 PM in the evening, Mr. and Mrs. Zhang hosted a banquet at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to entertain the Envoy, his wife, and his staff, inviting the heads of various ministries and their wives, as well as senior officials from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, to accompany them. Over 30 people attended. The party ended happily at 10:00 PM. It is said that Mr. Leitão da Cunha is scheduled to leave Nanjing for Beiping by train on the night of the 22nd. (21st Central News Agency Dispatch) Photo of Brazilian Envoy Presenting Credentials (International Press)

Sir Arthur Salter Arrives in Guangzhou from Hong Kong, Visits Chen Jitang and Lin Yunge 16

Hong Kong: Sir Arthur Salter and his wife, accompanied by Mr. Younger, arrived in Guangzhou from Hong Kong aboard the Taishan at 7:30 AM on the 21st. Mr. Scott, the British Commercial Commissioner in Hong Kong, traveled with them. Those who welcomed them upon arrival included Mr. Philip, the British Consul in Guangzhou, Mr. Zhou Xuetang, a representative from the Provincial and Municipal Government Headquarters, and Mr. Xiong Shaokang, Chairman of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, among others. Sir Arthur and Mr. Philip returned to the Consulate to rest. At 2:00 PM, they visited Chen Jitang, Lin Yunge, and Ji Wen, for ordinary social calls. At 3:00 PM, Chen Jitang and others went to the Consulate to return the visit. At 7:00 PM, Chen Jitang and Lin Yunge hosted a banquet at the Guesthouse. The Political Council and the Banking Association are scheduled to host a banquet on the 22nd. Sir Arthur is scheduled to visit the construction sites on the 23rd, and attend a banquet hosted by Liu Jiwen at 1:00 PM. He will return to Hong Kong on the 24th. (21st Central News Agency Dispatch)

Hong Kong: Sir Arthur Salter and his wife, accompanied by the British economist Mr. Younger, and the British Commercial Commissioner Mr. Scott, arrived in Guangzhou at 7:30 AM aboard the Taishan, and stayed at the British Consulate. At 2:00 PM, Sir Arthur and the British Consul visited Xiao Focheng, Zou Lu, and Li Zongren at the Political Council, and then visited Chen Jitang at the Headquarters, and Lin Yunge, Liu Jiwen, and Gan Jiehou at the Guangdong-Guangxi Negotiating Office of the Provincial and Municipal Government. At 3:00 PM, Xiao, Zou, Li, Chen, Lin, and others went to the Guesthouse to return the visit. In the evening, the Provincial Government hosted a banquet for Sir Arthur and others. It is said that Sir Arthur's mission is: 1. To balance the exchange rates between Hong Kong and Shanghai, and 2. To promote the connection of the Guangdong-Hankou and Guangzhou-Kowloon railways. Mr. Liao, the head of the Guangxi Bank of the Gui Clique, arrived in Guangdong to meet with Sir Arthur Salter. The Guangzhou Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a telegram on the 20th, opposing the connection of the Guangdong-Hankou and Guangzhou-Kowloon railways. The Provincial Assembly and the Guangdong Merchants Federation will also send similar telegrams. (21st Dispatch)

Guangzhou: Sir Arthur Salter, the British government's economic advisor, arrived here this morning aboard the Taishan with his wife, the financial expert Mr. Younger from the Hong Kong government, and the acting commercial commissioner, Mr. Scott. Chen Jitang, Lin Yunge, and Liu Jiwen all sent representatives to welcome them. Sir Arthur and others are staying at the British Consulate in Guangzhou. After arriving in the province, they met with British merchants in Guangzhou to hear their opinions on the current state of British trade in South China. They then called on the leaders of the southwest region. The Chinese-language newspapers here have paid considerable attention to Sir Arthur's trip. The official newspaper, the Shimin Daily, editorialized that it hoped that Sir Arthur's work would not only help to unify China's currency, but also establish concrete methods to restore Sino-British trade in South China, because Sino-British trade has declined due to the dumping of Japanese goods, and will continue to decline in the future. Chinese public opinion generally believes that Sir Arthur will discuss with the authorities how to improve economic relations between Guangzhou and Hong Kong, and study the general economic situation in Guangzhou. Due to Sir Arthur's arrival in the province, Chinese merchants are now actively promoting their opposition to the connection of the Guangzhou-Kowloon Railway and the Guangdong-Hankou Railway. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce has appealed to the Provincial Government and the Provincial Party Department to reject the discussion of the railway connection issue, because the Chamber of Commerce believes that if the railway connection is implemented, Guangzhou will become a dead port. Chinese newspapers report that the rumor that Sir Arthur will visit Guangxi Province is inaccurate according to Reuters. Sir Arthur is scheduled to return to Hong Kong on Sunday. Chen Jitang and Lin Yunge are scheduled to host a banquet tonight to entertain him. (21st Reuters Dispatch)

Gu Weijun Telegrams Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Postponing Trip to France Due to Illness 17

Nanjing: Gu Weijun, the Ambassador to France, was originally scheduled to depart on the 22nd, but telegraphed a report to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs that he had suddenly contracted a cold and fever reaching 103 degrees Fahrenheit. He has been admitted to Hongen Hospital for treatment. If his illness can be cured quickly, he will depart on the second sailing. At present, it is still difficult to determine the date of departure. (21st Dispatch)

New British Ambassador Sir Archibald Clark Kerr Soon to Arrive in China 18

Nanjing diplomatic sources: British Ambassador Sir Hughe Knatchbull-Hugessen has been transferred to Europe and will return home in April. The vacancy will be filled by Sir Archibald Clark Kerr, who will depart for China in the near future. Sir Archibald is currently 50 years old. He entered the diplomatic service in 1908. He served with the British delegation at the Paris Peace Conference in 1919. In the same year, he was promoted to the rank of First Secretary. In 1923, he was promoted to the rank of Counselor. From 1930 to 1934, he served as the British Envoy to Estonia, Latvia, Lithuania, and other countries. He is currently the British Envoy to Iran. (21st Central News Agency Dispatch)

Tianjin Shipping Industry Rescues Those Trapped 20

Tianjin experienced heavy snowfall all day on the 21st, accumulating over a foot, making transportation difficult. The situation for the ships trapped by ice at Dagukou is becoming increasingly critical. The Tianjin shipping industry held another meeting, appointing Wang Gengsan and Dong Haoyun to visit the Tianjin Customs Commissioner and the Director of the Haihe Engineering Bureau to request immediate rescue measures. It was decided that the two agencies would continue to rent the British icebreaker "Malara" and the Japanese icebreaker "奉天丸" to start work on the 22nd. On the 21st, due to the extreme cold, the submarine cable outside Dagukou was frozen and destroyed. The Tianjin Electric Bureau discussed hiring the Tianxing ship to break the ice and carry workers for repairs, but it was unsuccessful due to the thickness of the ice. Tianjin port's Shanghai and international telegrams were switched to landlines. (Special dispatch on the 21st)

Regarding the freezing of Dagukou in Tianjin, the Tianjin shipping industry telegraphed the Ministry of Communications and forwarded it to the Ministry of Finance, ordering Tianjin Customs to rescue the ice-trapped ships. There was still no reply on the 21st. The Customs Port Authority and the Haihe Engineering Bureau shirked responsibility, all claiming it was due to the weather and wind direction, and that it would thaw when it warmed up, and could not be rescued by human effort. Only after negotiations by the shipping industry on the 21st did they agree to rent British and Japanese icebreakers for rescue, with the expenses borne by the two agencies. (Special dispatch on the 21st)

A strong northeasterly wind is blowing in Tianjin, and the coast of North China is now frozen again. More than a dozen ships are trapped by ice outside Dagukou Bay, including ten Chinese merchant ships. The Chinese Shipping Association has appealed to the central government for relief. The thickest ice is said to be 40 feet thick, extending ten miles from Dagukou Bay, with ice floes 20 feet high and 120 feet long and wide. The Taikoo ships "Yuezhou" and another ship set off from Tanggu yesterday, traveling only two miles all day. Tugs are now planning to approach the trapped ships to provide supplies. If they cannot reach them, they will use coolies to transport food. One icebreaker disembarked a hundred passengers from a certain Japanese ship today, but due to the difficulty of navigation, it has not yet reached the shore. (Reuters dispatch on the 21st)

The Japanese military in Tianjin has decided to cooperate with the Economic Committee of the Hebei-Chahar Political Council to send Manchurian and South Manchuria Railway employees as rural instructors. The Executive Yuan Warns All Staff of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company 24

The Executive Yuan, under President Jiang, has issued a public notice to all officers and staff of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, urging them to abide by discipline. The full text is as follows:

Public Notice: The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has the longest history and largest scale among shipping organizations in our country. However, due to poor management over the years, its business has declined and its debts have increased day by day. This continuous loss must be reversed. Since its nationalization in recent years, although it has been striving for better management, the results are still minimal. The Executive Yuan has decided to order the Ministry of Communications to reorganize the company, revise its organizational charter, and provide guidance on rectification methods, with the intention of eliminating corruption, eradicating the long-standing habits of embezzlement and perfunctory behavior, and implementing a thorough reform. Such measures should be understood and appreciated by those who understand the situation. All employees of the company, who have served for a long time and are familiar with the situation, should, if they have any insights on how to eliminate long-standing malpractices, improve business operations, and start increasing revenue and reducing expenditures, submit them to their superiors for consideration. If they do not follow the correct path, but stubbornly insist on their own opinions, or even succumb to the temptation of external malicious elements, sow discord, incite unrest, and affect the company's operations, the President of the Executive Yuan will regard this as a violation of discipline and disruption of transportation, and will severely punish them according to the law without any leniency. In addition, if employees of various branches, warehouses, and docks engage in such behavior, they will be dealt with equally. In addition to ordering the Ministry of Communications to earnestly supervise, quickly report on the rectification, this notice is hereby issued for public knowledge. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 21st)

Jia Degan Recalled to the Ministry; British Ambassador to China Replaced; Xu Zhisen, Envoy to Persia, Succeeds Jia, a Talented Diplomat, Promoted to Deputy Undersecretary of State 27

London: Sir Jia Degan, the British Ambassador to China, has succeeded Sir Wellesley, who retired due to old age, as Deputy Undersecretary of State for Foreign Affairs. His vacant post will be filled by Sir Xu Zhisen, the British Envoy to Iran (Persia) since 1934, which has been approved by the British Emperor. Xu was born in 1886, studied at Oxford, and entered the diplomatic service in 1908. In January 1919, he served on the British delegation to the Paris Peace Conference. In the same year, he was promoted to First Secretary of the Foreign Office. From 1926 to 1930, he served as Counselor at the British Embassy in Belgium. From 1930 to 1934, he served as Envoy to several Balkan countries. After that, he was transferred to Envoy to Iran. He has one son and two daughters. (Reuters dispatch on the 20th)

London: The new appointment of Sir Jia Degan was welcomed by The Times and the Daily Telegraph today. The Times stated that the Foreign Office would become more powerful as a result. The Daily Telegraph stated that Jia Degan served as the head of the League of Nations section for several years before becoming Ambassador to China. His promotion to Deputy Undersecretary of State shows not only his talent but also Foreign Secretary Eden's desire to pursue his League of Nations policy. (Reuters dispatch on the 21st)

Japanese Attendant at the Naval Conference, Major General Iwashita, Returns to Yokohama 29

Yokohama: Major General Iwashita, the naval attendant at the London Naval Disarmament Conference, returned to Yokohama on the Asama Maru at 8:00 a.m. on the 21st. (Domei News Agency dispatch on the 21st)

Naval Conference Work to End After Political Negotiations Conclude; Only a Technical Agreement Will Be Initialed; Invitation to Germany to Participate Still Faces Difficulties 30

London: Naval sources predict that the Naval Conference will conclude its work in the middle of next week. At that time, only a technical agreement will be initialed, and no treaty is likely to be signed. Even this technical agreement must be implemented after the current political negotiations conclude. The current difficulty lies in the issue of inviting Germany to sign and participate. The United Kingdom believes that the sooner the better, while France insists that air security and naval disarmament should be linked, and Germany can only be invited to participate after this principle is recognized. The United States still believes that naval issues are purely technical and should not involve political issues. These are the general attitudes of the three countries. As for the issue of battleship tonnage, it is unlikely to hinder the initialing of the agreement, because the current compromise plan, which sets the battleship tonnage at 35,000 tons but limits it to five years, is acceptable to all countries. (Havas dispatch on the 20th)

US Representative Meets with Eden, Optimistic About Conference Prospects

London: The US chief representative to the Naval Conference, Davis, met with British Foreign Secretary Eden today and expressed concern about the delay in the conference due to political issues. However, Eden told him that the conference would focus on purely naval matters and would not be unduly prolonged. The French Ambassador to the UK, Corbin, did not visit Eden. The French Ambassador is currently awaiting instructions from Paris regarding France's request to Washington to reduce warship tonnage and other matters. (Reuters dispatch on the 21st)

London: Foreign Secretary Eden met with the US chief representative to the Naval Conference, Norman Davis, today to discuss the situation of the conference. US officials here are now expressing optimism about the prospects of the conference. However, according to general opinion, the only realistic hope for the future is that a technical agreement can be reached in the middle of next week. (Havas dispatch on the 20th)

Negotiations on Qualitative Restrictions Underway; Talk of Expanding the Scope of the Naval Conference

Regarding the issue of qualitative naval restrictions, the countries involved are currently conducting political negotiations. Once these negotiations are concluded, a new naval conference may be convened here, with the participation of the UK, the US, France, Italy, Germany, and Russia. The UK will contact Japan to invite its attendance, and if agreed, Japan will also participate in the conference. It was rumored yesterday that Italy would make the revocation of sanctions a condition for signing a future naval treaty. Naval officials here have mixed feelings about this news and will likely wait until the Italian representatives to the Naval Conference, Rainaldi and Piccia, return from Rome before the truth becomes clear. (Havas dispatch on the 20th)

Washington: The French Ambassador to the United States, de Laboulaye, previously discussed the issue of battleship tonnage with Deputy Secretary of State Phillips. It is understood that the US government did not directly respond to de Laboulaye's proposals because the negotiations currently underway in London are friendly and seamless and will likely achieve a satisfactory resolution. The US government is keen to avoid anything that could cause misunderstanding and suggest that naval negotiations could be moved from London to Washington. (Havas dispatch on the 20th)

Committee of Experts Concludes Work; Methods for Qualitative Restrictions Agreed Upon

London: The General Committee of the Naval Conference previously appointed a subcommittee of experts to study the issue of qualitative restrictions on various warships (excluding battleships). The subcommittee has recently concluded its work and agreed on the following restrictions:

* Aircraft carriers: 22,000 tons, with guns of 6-inch caliber.

* Class A cruisers: 10,000 tons, with guns of 8-inch and 6-inch caliber.

* Class B cruisers: 7,500 tons, with guns of 6-inch caliber.

* Destroyers and light cruisers are classified as one category. Destroyers are set at 1,850 tons, with guns of 5-inch caliber.

* Submarines: 2,000 tons, with guns of 4-inch caliber.

* Other small warships, such as shallow-water defense ships, which were originally not subject to qualitative restrictions under the Washington Naval Treaty, will continue to be unrestricted in the future. However, countries will notify each other when constructing them. Also, the number of aircraft carried by various warships that are not classified as aircraft carriers will not be restricted. The definition of aircraft carriers remains the same as that contained in the Washington Naval Treaty, i.e., any vessel equipped with a flight deck and equipment to assist in the launch of aircraft will be considered an aircraft carrier. However, the current definition is more detailed. (Havas dispatch on the 20th)

British Defense Plan Adjusts Working Procedures of the Army, Navy and Air Force; To Be Formally Announced in Parliament Soon 31

London: In the House of Commons today, there was questioning about newspaper disclosures regarding the British defense plan. Prime Minister Baldwin replied that the defense plan had not been leaked to the outside world. The information in the newspapers was only based on informed predictions and factual knowledge. He said that if he had the position and knowledge of an ordinary journalist, he could also write it. The defense plan will soon be announced in Parliament, which includes adjusting the working procedures of the Army, Navy and Air Force, and paying attention to the proper functions of these three departments in this procedure. However, any long-term procedure must be flexible and must be constantly modified as needed by the environment. As for the nature of the command, he was not prepared to elaborate until the defense debate. When a member asked about the increase in the purchase price of armaments, Baldwin replied that the air force procurement contract contains a purchase price clause, and this will continue to be followed in the future to prevent contractors from obtaining excessive profits in army and navy contracts. Baldwin also said that he would move on Monday to suspend discussion of other matters in the House of Commons to focus on debating foreign policy. He hoped that this debate could be completed by 9:30 p.m., and then consider the supplementary budgets for the Army, Navy and Air Force. (Reuters dispatch on the 20th)

Secret Documents Leaked; London Investigates the Truth; UK's Sanctions Against Italy Are Not Self-Serving; Moffat Report Provides Powerful Evidence 34

London: Sir Moffat, Permanent Under-Secretary of State for the Colonies, was ordered last spring to study the interests of the United Kingdom in Abyssinia, as to how they would be affected by Italy's policy toward Abyssinia. He submitted a report, the contents of which have not been made public until yesterday, when an Italian newspaper published a summary. It is now known that Foreign Secretary Eden will make a statement to the House of Commons on Monday, commenting on the report. As far as this agency knows, the report only studies the Abyssinian issue from a number of perspectives. The full text is 12,000 words long and is marked "Secret" on the cover, with the words "Property of the British Government." Cabinet members, senior officials of the relevant departments, the British Embassy in Italy, and agencies in British territories in Africa who contributed opinions to the government each received a copy. It is generally believed that the attitude adopted by the United Kingdom toward Italy in the Italo-Ethiopian dispute does not contain any imperialistic notions. This is powerfully evidenced in Sir Moffat's report. Therefore, the Cabinet may decide to publish the original text of the report. (Havas News Agency dispatch on the 20th)

London: Government officials began investigating the truth today about how the Italian newspaper obtained the secret report of the Moffat Committee. They did not express outrage at the Italian newspaper's disclosure of this secret document, but merely stated that it was sufficient proof that the United Kingdom's demand for League of Nations sanctions against Italy had no selfish motives. A government spokesman said today that since the Italian Embassy Counselor in the UK, Vedetti, informed British officials on January 29 last year of the secret agreement between Italian Prime Minister Mussolini and former French Foreign Minister Laval, the UK immediately appointed a committee to investigate the facts but not to make any recommendations. Subsequently, because the British Cabinet did not believe that Italy's aggression against Abyssinia would infringe on British interests, the report of the committee has not been adopted. (Guomin News Agency dispatch on the 20th)

London: Today, members of the House of Commons questioned Prime Minister Baldwin about the Italian newspaper's publication of the secret report of the Colonial Office Undersecretary Moffat in June 1935, which stated the UK's attitude toward Italy's rights in Abyssinia and stated that Italy's actions in Abyssinia were not of major concern to British interests. Conservative Party member Churchill was eager to know how the London Office's affairs were leaked to the outside world. Labour Party member Lansbury said that if the House of Commons did not know all the facts before Monday, it could not debate foreign affairs. Baldwin replied that he was very busy this morning and had not read the newspapers, that he would pay attention to the matter, but could not answer at this time. (Reuters dispatch on the 20th)

London: According to unofficial investigations today, the secret report of the British Colonial Office official Moffat, which was disclosed by the Italian newspaper in Rome yesterday, was actually obtained by Italy through improper means. British Foreign Secretary Eden will explain this matter in the House of Commons on Monday. It is heard that the government may decide to publish this document. (Reuters dispatch on the 21st)

French Chamber of Deputies Continues Debate on Franco-Soviet Mutual Assistance Pact: Herriot Defends 36

Paris - Former leader of the Radical Socialist Party, Herriot, spoke in the Chamber of Deputies today to defend the Franco-Soviet Mutual Assistance Treaty, saying, "Regarding the collective security system, the interests of the Soviet Union are no different from ours. We must not judge the foreign policy of a country based on observations of its internal affairs. After the Franco-Soviet Mutual Assistance Treaty, France's responsibility for Central Europe can be somewhat reduced, which is undeniable. Moreover, since the Soviet Union joined the League of Nations, its representatives have cooperated in all the League's affairs. I am deeply convinced of its sincerity. As for France, it should remain loyal to the principles of arbitration, security, and disarmament, and never waver." Herriot then said that the French and Russian peoples should abandon their prejudices and be in harmony, saying, "The Soviet Union has a vast land and a large population, and there is ample room for intellectual development. As a humble descendant of the French Revolution, I sincerely hope that the two great revolutions of France and Russia will be harmonized. The Franco-Soviet Mutual Assistance Treaty does not harm or threaten any country. Its conclusion does not go beyond the scope of the League of Nations, and it is also in line with the provisions of the Locarno Pact. Our responsibility in Central Europe can be eased, and the two great nations of France and Russia can be brought closer. This is why I ask the members of the Chamber of Deputies to pass it." After his speech, the Chamber immediately announced an adjournment and scheduled to continue the debate next Tuesday. (Havas dispatch on the 20th)

Paris - The Chamber of Deputies met today to continue discussing the ratification of the Franco-Soviet Mutual Assistance Treaty. A Communist member, Doriot, stood up to speak, denouncing the dual policy of the Soviet government and the Third International as dangerous and sharply criticized it, moving the listeners. He said briefly that the Franco-Soviet Mutual Assistance Treaty might drag France into a whirlpool of war, "and as a result, the Third International, for the sake of fomenting revolution, may abandon us midway and discard us like worn-out shoes. France is a democratic country, and its policy is based on the Treaty of Versailles and the collective security system. The Soviet Union, since its founding by Lenin, has called for world revolution, which is a unique country. The Soviet government and the Third International are two in one, although they have different names, the power is in one hand. Those who manipulate this dual policy are far-sighted and difficult to fathom. The political systems of France and Russia are contrary to each other, and the national conditions are different. One intends to destroy the other's social system. How is it possible to force them to connect and conclude such a treaty? We really cannot understand. "Doriot then described the changes in Soviet policy since German leader Hitler came to power, saying that the Soviet Union regarded National Socialism as a great enemy of the Soviet system, so it reversed its previous diplomatic position and turned to using the antagonism of the imperialist countries such as France and its allies towards National Socialism to confront Germany. The Soviet Union simply took advantage of the fact that the defeated countries in the European War changed their political systems, and immediately put itself in the ranks of the victorious countries to exclude these defeated countries. This plan is enough to cause war," and so on. (Note: Doriot was originally one of the leaders of the French Communist Party. In May of the previous year, he advocated uniting the Socialist Party to resist Fascism, which led to conflicts with the Third International and the French Communist Party cadres. He then united with some party members to form an independent Communist Party.) (Havas dispatch on the 20th)

Diplomatic Activities Among Italy, Germany, and Poland: Discussions Limited to European Issues 37

Paris - According to news obtained by the Morning Post's correspondent in Rome, the Polish Ambassador to Italy, Wyszynski, held talks with Prime Minister Mussolini yesterday afternoon, and then spoke with Polish Foreign Minister Colonel Beck on the phone, and then set off for home that evening. It is heard that when Prime Minister Mussolini of Italy met with German Ambassador Hassell and Polish Ambassador Wyszynski, he informed them of Italy's views on the Danube River issue. When Italian Foreign Minister Suvich met with Austrian Foreign Minister Weikersheim in Florence some days ago, he also explained this view. This is the reason for the sudden increase in diplomatic activity between Italy, Germany, and Poland recently. However, it is limited to issues related to Europe. The two issues of the redistribution of mandated territories and Germany's external economic expansion, which are wider in scope, do not seem to have been touched upon. (Havas dispatch on the 21st)

Development of Railway Transportation Between the Soviet Union and Iran: Building New Roads to Facilitate Travel, Track Width Standardized 38

Moscow - Railways will soon be built between the Soviet Union and Iran (i.e., Persia), from the capital of the Armenian state in southeastern Soviet Union, Yerevan, to the city of Tabriz in Iran, so that the two countries can be directly connected by rail. In the future, the line will be extended from Tabriz to the Iranian capital to develop transportation between the two countries. Currently, those who go to Iran must hire vehicles in addition to taking the train, which is extremely inconvenient. In the future, when new roads are built, the width of the tracks, whether in the Soviet Union or in Iran, will be standardized so that people can travel directly back and forth without having to change trains at the border between the two countries. According to the Imperial Russian era, the Russian government never allowed the width of its tracks to be the same as those of other European countries. There were various reasons for this. The most important reason was that in the event of war, it would be difficult for foreign troops to use the railway to enter the country. (Havas Telegraph Agency dispatch on the 21st)

Page 9

Japanese General Election: First Day of Vote Counting, Minseito Party Clearly Dominates, Suzuki Loses Seat in Unexpected Turn 39

Tokyo - The opening of the vote counting for the fourth general election, reflecting the general will of the people, was held simultaneously at 8:00 a.m. today. The vote counting was completed today. The results have been determined for 62 districts, with 239 elected representatives. Partial vote counts have been conducted in 54 districts, and the remaining 122 districts will also be completed by the morning of the 23rd. (Dentsu dispatch on the 21st)

Tokyo - In the first day's election vote count, many new faces from the Minseito Party and the proletarian parties were crowned, while the opposition Seiyukai Party was in a difficult position, extremely pessimistic. However, the districts where the votes were counted on the first day were originally the city centers where the Minseito Party had an advantage. Therefore, the results as of 5:30 p.m. show that the Minseito Party had 51 seats, the Seiyukai Party 29, and the Shakai Taishuto 12. If the vote counting in the counties on the 22nd cannot show an unexpected turnaround, the old dream of the Seiyukai Party being the largest party may be shattered. However, the difference in the number of seats for the so-called largest party is very small. At this point, the highest number of votes obtained was by proletarian party member Kato Kanju, with more than 53,000 votes, which is attracting widespread attention. (Domei News Agency dispatch on the 21st)

Tokyo - As of 11:00 p.m. on the 21st, the number of representatives elected from each party is as follows:

Minsei 102, Seiyu 79, Shakai Taishuto 15, Showa 11, Kokumin Domei 3, Other Parties 3, Independent 9, Total 222. (Domei News Agency dispatch on the 21st)

Tokyo - (Sent at 4:41 a.m.) The latest results of the Japanese election are as follows: Minsei 109 seats, Seiyukai 78 seats, Shakai Taishuto 15 seats, Showa 11 seats, Kokumin Domei 4 seats, Independent 13 seats, Total 229 seats. (Reuters dispatch on the 22nd)

Tokyo - Seiyukai President Suzuki Kisaburo lost the election in the second district of Kanagawa. Mr. Kawaguchi Yoshihisa (former Seiyukai member) of the district will resign his seat and hand it over to President Suzuki. (Domei News Agency dispatch on the 21st)

Tokyo - The results of the general election, which began counting votes at 8:00 a.m. today, are gradually becoming clear under the attention of the entire nation. However, during the vote counting, unexpected waves were stirred up in various places by the progress of the proletarian parties, which is enough to disrupt the existing party lineup. They have been obtaining the highest number of votes everywhere. Although it is not yet a problem in terms of the total number, the victory of these new faces from the proletarian parties is quite unexpected. Therefore, many former members of the Seiyukai and Minseito Parties have been defeated, which is quite noteworthy. As for the struggle between the Seiyukai and Minseito Parties, in the 62 districts with 239 seats where the vote counting ended in the first ten days, the Minseito Party slightly dominates. The vote counting in the county districts will be held tomorrow. It is still difficult to predict whether it will be a victory for the Minseito Party or whether the opposition parties will maintain their existing strength. (Domei News Agency dispatch on the 21st)

Two Earthquakes in Osaka, Forty Casualties 40

Osaka - A major earthquake occurred in Osaka and Kyoto at 10:10 this morning, with tremors lasting for one minute. Telegraph and telephone lines were cut off, and two or three fires broke out in Osaka City. (Domei dispatch on the 21st)

Osaka - At 1:05 p.m. today (Japan time), Osaka experienced another strong earthquake, causing extreme anxiety among the people. (Dentsu dispatch on the 21st)

Tokyo - The Osaka earthquake lasted 9.3 seconds and caused more than ten fires, but they were quickly extinguished and did not spread. Telephone and telegraph lines were disrupted. Three workers died after falling from a tall chimney they were working on, and in another incident, eleven people were crushed to death by a landslide. (Reuters dispatch on the 21st)

Tokyo - Kobe also felt the earthquake, and Nagoya also felt a slight tremor. Kobe seems to have suffered only minor damage, but it is reported that there are many casualties in Osaka. (Reuters dispatch on the 21st)

Osaka - As of 11:00 a.m. today, the damage caused by this morning's earthquake has been determined to be as follows: Three workers in Nishiyodogawa Ward died after falling while repairing a chimney due to the strong earthquake. In Minamikawachi County, 22 houses were completely or partially destroyed, and two people died. (Dentsu dispatch on the 21st)

Osaka - As of 11:00 a.m., the earthquake damage investigated is as follows: Ten houses collapsed in Kashiwara Town outside the city, injuring more than ten people. Twelve fires broke out in the city and are currently spreading. Other damage is minor. (Domei News Agency dispatch on the 21st)

Osaka - According to a report received by the Osaka Police Department, the damage caused by the earthquake in Osaka City is as follows: 21 houses collapsed, 17 houses partially collapsed, 5 deaths, 16 injuries, 12 fires, 3 water pipe bursts. (Domei News Agency dispatch on the 21st)

Osaka - The Osaka Prefectural Police Department's report on the damage caused by today's earthquake, as of 6:00 p.m., is as follows: 8 deaths, 8 serious injuries, 24 minor injuries, 15 houses completely collapsed, 29 houses partially collapsed, 2 water pipe breaks, 3 iron bridge destructions, 2 chimney collapses, 2 fires. In Goji Town, Nara Prefecture, which was buried by a landslide, after the efforts of firefighters and youth groups, 8 seriously injured people have been rescued, but 2 have died. (Dentsu dispatch on the 21st)

Tokyo - According to the Central Meteorological Observatory, at 10:08 a.m. on the 21st, a rare earthquake occurred in the Kansai region, but there was no feeling in Tokyo. The epicenter was near the Kongo Mountain foothills and the Yamato River basin on the border between Osaka and Nara Prefectures. The earthquake's magnitude cannot yet be considered a major earthquake, and is roughly the same as the Shizuoka earthquake on July 22 of last year. The affected area is relatively small, with the strong tremor area being the Kinki region, the weak tremor area extending west to Okayama and east to Hamamatsu, and the slight tremor area extending from Beppu in Aeta east to Mishima. The intensity of the earthquake varies depending on the strength of the ground in the Kinki region. Osaka, Kyoto, Wakayama, Nara Prefecture, etc., have a higher intensity of tremors. (Domei News Agency dispatch on the 21st)

Supporter of the Emperor Organ Theory, Dr. Minobe Tatsukichi, Assassinated: Assailant Related to Right-Wing Daito Society, Shot and Arrested by Police on the Spot 41

Tokyo - Dr. Minobe was shot by a thug with a handgun at his home in Kichijoji this morning and sustained a serious injury to his right leg. The perpetrator was arrested immediately. (Domei News Agency dispatch on the 21st)

Tokyo - The assailant who attacked Dr. Minobe, named Oda, used a letter of introduction to see Minobe at 15 minutes past the hour. As soon as he entered the room, he took out a gun from his bag and fired several shots. Minobe was injured in his left leg and shouted for help. Police officers who heard the noise entered the room and shot the assailant. It is reported that the assailant was seriously injured and was sent to the police station for a long interrogation. Minobe was taken to the hospital for treatment, but his injuries are not serious. (Reuters dispatch on the 21st)

Tokyo - The perpetrator who shot at Dr. Minobe, Oda Jujiro, used a letter of introduction from the doctor's assistant to meet the doctor. Dr. Minobe received him in the living room upstairs. During the conversation, Oda suddenly fired at the doctor with a handgun, and the bullet hit his right leg. Because the doctor raised his voice and called for help, the police officer on guard rushed to the scene and fought with the perpetrator, injuring him and arresting him. Dr. Minobe was immediately taken to the Imperial University Hospital. His life is not in danger. The perpetrator was taken to the Tanashi Police Station for questioning. He said that he is currently unemployed and has connections with the right-wing group Daito Society. (Domei News Agency dispatch on the 21st)

New Spanish Prime Minister Announces Policy Platform: Maintaining Social Order Based on the Constitution, Amnesty for Political Prisoners, Implementation of Agricultural Policies 42

Madrid - The new Prime Minister Azana recently gave a speech to the people via radio broadcast, saying, "The policy program adopted by the new government is based on peace, justice, and freedom. I hereby appeal to all citizens of the country for peace, and I sincerely hope that the people will live up to the government's expectations." He also said, "The government will now implement its policy platform, which is no different from what it proclaimed during the election campaign, and the wounds suffered by the left-wing in the past will be remedied first." The Prime Minister then said that the cabinet had decided to immediately restore the municipal councils across the country (i.e., those elected on April 12, 1931, which were ordered to be dissolved by the government after the failure of the October Revolution two years ago). The cabinet will also compensate for the illegal treatment received by civil servants under previous governments, and hopes that the amnesty decree will be issued soon. In conclusion, he said, "We sincerely hope that all those who assist us in restoring the republican system will not disturb public order in the future, so as not to tarnish the victory we have achieved, even if the motive is pure, we must be cautious. In short, all Spanish people, regardless of party affiliation, should be treated fairly so that the country can be revitalized." The government is currently drafting a major amnesty bill, which will be submitted to the new Chamber of Deputies for discussion. In addition, there are several other bills related to agricultural reform, which will also be submitted to the Chamber of Deputies for review. At this time, the government also intends to ask the Standing Committee of the Chamber of Deputies to release all political prisoners who have not yet been sentenced. (Havas dispatch on the 20th)

Madrid - The new government recently issued a public announcement via radio broadcast, saying, "The cabinet is scheduled to hold a cabinet meeting this morning to discuss the issue of amnesty for political prisoners, and will immediately ask the President to order the Standing Committee of the Chamber of Deputies to allow the cabinet to issue substitute legal orders, so that all political and social criminals and all members of parliament from the Basque province who were sentenced for participating in the October Revolution two years ago will be pardoned. Although the representatives of various political parties in the Standing Committee may have fundamental disagreements on the issue of amnesty due to party differences, the cabinet still hopes that they will eventually agree to it." The Standing Committee is now scheduled to hold its first meeting today, and will finalize the vote on the major amnesty bill on Saturday and Sunday. (Havas dispatch on the 21st)

Madrid - Spain is now gradually becoming tranquil, but in a few places, left-wing members have taken extra-legal actions due to the election victory. Riots have occurred in Alicante Province and Murcia in southeastern Spain. The offices of the Catholic Party and its newspapers have been destroyed, and a monastery has been set on fire. The authorities have issued martial law. In Braziloban, a demonstration was held by the Socialist Party and the Communist Party, which clashed with the police. The police opened fire, resulting in twelve injuries. (Reuters dispatch on the 21st)

Filipinos in America Granted Military Training: Proposal by Democratic Congressman 43

Washington - Democratic Congressman Dingell told the Associated Press today that he will propose in the House of Representatives tomorrow to allow 100 Filipinos to receive training in American naval and military academies. Dingell said that after the United States withdraws from the Philippines, the Philippines should be prepared to protect its independence without seeking American assistance. His proposal will stipulate that in the first semester after the bill is passed, 25 Filipinos will be selected from West Point Military Academy and Annapolis Naval Academy, and then 5 Filipinos will be selected each year for a period of five years. Dingell said that after these people graduate, they can become leading officers in command of the Philippine scouts and constabulary, and can also teach other officers. Dingell has always paid attention to Philippine affairs. According to him, the bill was not initiated by the army and navy, but was his own initiative. (Kokumin dispatch on the 20th)

The Hague - The Dutch Foreign Minister today defended to the Upper House the government's reasons for not restoring diplomatic relations with the Soviet Union. Foreign Minister Gaeff said that if the government were to recognize the Soviet Union, the Netherlands would become a hotbed for communist propaganda and activities. U.S. Senate Passes Bill to Control Arms Transportation 47

Washington - The Senate today passed a bill to control the interstate transportation of arms, in order to prevent thugs from obtaining weapons. The bill has now been sent to the House of Representatives. At the same time, members of the Senate Arms Investigation Committee have gained a deep understanding of arms transportation after listening to the statement of Philadelphia arms merchant Strauss. Strauss said that thugs never buy weapons from people, but his own arms factory had been robbed three times by organized bandits, and many handguns and machine guns had been stolen. Hat manufacturer Barrett also told the committee that he had engaged in arms trading as a sideline, and had previously purchased 3,500 old machine guns for only 12 cents each, and later sold them for 7.75 dollars each. However, after discovering that these old guns could be used with a little repair, he stopped selling them. Now, he only sells to licensed individuals. Any revolutionaries can purchase these arms from the United States. (Kokumin dispatch on the 20th)

They hope that the genuine press in Japan will also exert its courage and power to jointly save the crisis of peace in East Asia and expressed their sincere respect for Yamamoto. Finally, Yamamoto expressed his willingness to accept the opinions of the Chinese press and expressed his sincere gratitude. The discussion was harmonious and ended at 6:00 PM. The costs will be borne by the provinces holding the examinations. For remote or financially difficult provinces, the Ministry plans to request central government subsidies. The first measure has already been approved by the Examination Yuan, while the second measure has been resolved by the Central Political Council to change the examination expenses to be borne by the provinces holding the examinations, but financially difficult or border provinces may request appropriate subsidies from the central government. Heavy Snow and Extremely Cold Weather in Beiping 72

An Account of Life in Semo (8) 102

— Jin Dui

"Can ordinary people even get newspapers?" It was morning again, on the way back to my residence from Maying—the former site of the Ningxia Provincial Government—I saw a shop front piled high with fresh "large pancakes." This was a rare sight for us who had always lived in schools in the interior. We had already resolved to adapt to the northwestern lifestyle in order to get a real understanding of the situation. Therefore, we decided to have a northwestern-style breakfast today: buy a couple of scallion oil pancakes to fill our stomachs. I picked out a few of the steaming pancakes from the stall, made a small pile, and paid the money. But these greasy and spicy pancakes could not be eaten on the street. So I asked the pancake seller for a paper to wrap them in. I naturally thought that old newspapers would be the most suitable. "Do ordinary people in our homes even have newspapers?" This sentence, which seemed to be a well-reasoned argument, was the shopkeeper's way of refusing to provide a paper wrap. It turns out that the underdevelopment of the newspaper industry in Ningxia is undeniable. There is only one newspaper office, and the daily circulation is small. Besides government agencies, only a very few people subscribe. So, newspapers are naturally not found in ordinary people's homes. We could only sigh at the backwardness of northwestern culture.

"Come to Ningxia to marry a concubine." Due to the geographical environment, cultural development is lagging behind, the atmosphere is not yet open, and everything is immature. The education system is certainly no exception, especially women's education. There is only one girls' middle school in the entire city of Ningxia, offering junior high school and attached primary school. The number of students is also very small. Although students who enter the school are not only exempted from all tuition and miscellaneous fees, but also receive a monthly stipend of several dollars in addition to the supply of books, ultimately due to the closed atmosphere, parents stubbornly disapprove of their daughters showing their faces on the way to and from school. Poor families, although they do not have to spend money to attend school, are unwilling to leave their homes all day long. They still have to supplement some clothes and socks. They always want their daughters to help with some chores at home. They can also do some work that can earn a considerable profit. As for the girls who go to school, although many of them aim to seek knowledge, many of the students have other intentions. Doesn't entering school put them in the position of "female student"? "Female student," that's fashionable enough! The marriage problem is much easier to solve from then on. Therefore, as long as they succeed in marriage and find a satisfactory husband to rely on for life, they are willing to drop out of school. On the scale of their eyes, among the various occupations of agriculture, industry, commerce, military, politics, and police, they consider the figures mixed in the political arena to have the most important and highest status. Therefore, the ideal husbands of Ningxia women are mostly chosen from government employees. As long as the official position is high and important, they do not care whether it is a first marriage or a remarriage, and they are willing to be concubines even if they have a wife. It doesn't matter which wife they are, even if they are of questionable background, daughters from good families are still willing. Even after being deceived, divorced, or abandoned, they are willing to be deceived again. No wonder civil servants from other provinces all hold the view of "come to Ningxia to marry a concubine" and put this view into practice. This is truly a distorted phenomenon of women's education.

"Vow not to marry women with bound feet." In the past, the custom of foot binding was very prevalent among women in Ningxia. Foot binding is extremely inhumane and has a greater impact on the health of the nation. Recently, the educational authorities in Ningxia Province have also realized that this custom is bad and are promoting the natural foot movement. In addition to posting propaganda in the main thoroughfares to advise women and the public to unbind their feet, they also made a kind of armband with white cloth, red border, and black characters, rectangular in shape, printed with "Vow not to marry women with bound feet," and distributed it to unmarried primary and secondary school students throughout the city to wear. Sure enough, it was eye-catching and alerting. For the sake of their lifelong happiness, women's families and the women themselves have all implemented foot liberation. Therefore, in the provincial capital, you can no longer see girls under the age of fifteen or sixteen with small feet like the lotus steps of the past. This is a praiseworthy sight. It's just that among older women and in remote rural areas, the custom is still too strong, and there are still traces of bound feet staggering along.

A lifetime of three baths. "When a baby falls to the ground, the whole body is bathed for the first time. Only on the eve of the wedding night is the second bath performed. Afterwards, until death, the body bath at the time of encoffining is the third time. That is the last bath of life, and it is passive." An overseas Chinese businessman who has lived in Ningxia for many years told me the story of the locals "a lifetime of three baths." Perhaps it is an exaggeration, but it can also be seen that ordinary people do not pay attention to hygiene. Perhaps the climate has something to do with it. It is purely continental. The province is mostly desert, the air is dry, in the summer, dust accumulates on the streets, wind and dust fly. After washing clothes and body, they are immediately soiled again. Laziness is the nature of the northwestern people, so they simply let it go. Habit becomes nature. In winter, there is no rain but snow, and the wind is terribly cold. No one wants to expose their skin to wash. The common people are all draped in old sheepskin robes, felt shoes, and fur hats. The smell of scallions, garlic, and mutton emanates from their mouths and bodies. Thus, the lives of the locals are spent in this dirty environment all day long. Every day they lead donkeys, cows, or horses, perhaps camels, with goods on their backs, to the market to find their patrons.

Sleeping on a kang is like a smoking bed. Opium is one of Ningxia's products, even more important than fur. In the summer, in May and June, the fields are covered with all kinds of colorful flowers, that is the poppy season. Smoking opium has become an extremely common phenomenon in Ningxia. The production is high, the price is cheap. Except for Muslims who rarely have a liking for it, most families have a set of smoking equipment on the kang, and even replace fragrant tea with opium to entertain guests. In social gatherings, people in the middle and lower classes smoke even more. Men and women are equally qualified as "old guns." Poor laborers, whose homes are bare, but beyond the four walls, there is a smoking lamp. Sleeping on a kang is like a smoking bed. It is simply better to have no rice to cook than to have no smoke to live on. But once addicted to opium, the spirit is weakened, which also cultivates a lazy disposition and leads to panic in life.

More Than 300 Shops in Nanchang Closed Down Last Year - Statistics from the Public Security Bureau 103

Nanchang Correspondence. Jiangxi has suffered from economic decline and rural bankruptcy in recent years. All industries are in recession, and people's livelihood is withered, showing an unprecedented scene of panic. Nanchang City, the economic center of the province, has also seen commercial bankruptcy due to the people's lack of purchasing power. In the past year, the city was in a state of economic collapse that could hardly be contained. By the end of last year, more than 350 households had announced their closure and bankruptcy. It is feared that those managed by creditors, secretly closed, or in a state of suspended animation account for a quarter of the total. At present, the most prosperous Zhongzheng Road and Zhongshan Road are full of closed shops being rented, leased, and cleared out. Business this year is still cold, and the future is very pessimistic. The following is a list of the shops that closed down last year, according to the statistics of the Public Security Bureau: Chinese and Western medicine shops, 5; coal shops, 3; theaters and cinemas, 2; stationery and paper shops, 5; military clothing shops, 3; butchers, 6; Chinese and Western restaurants, 10; inns and hotels, 23; apartments, 12; porcelain shops, 3; shipping companies, 1; cloth shops, 8; silk, satin, cotton cloth and cotton yarn shops, 12; general merchandise stores of Jiangsu and Guangdong, 18; dyeing shops, 7; lacquer shops, 2; rice shops, 17; water and wine shops, 8; Ding Shao wine shops, 4; southern goods and Beijing confectionery shops, 24; bamboo and wood shops, 23; warehouses, 6; gold and silver shops, 5; noodle shops, 31; fried dough sticks and clear soup shops, tea shops, 19; printing shops, 3; rubber tire shops, 6; bookstores, 3; salt shops, 3; transport companies, 1; tofu shops, 3; egg shops, 1; special goods shops, 6; pig business shops, 1; ointment grinding shops, 1; shoe stores, 11; glass shops, 2; mounting and engraving shops, 5; pen and ink shops, 1; barber shops, 4; dental inlay shops, 1; liquor shops, 5; electrical material shops, 3; cotton shops, 3; chicken and duck shops, 2; incense shops, 1; rain gear shops, 1; used clothing shops, 1; construction companies, 2; soap shops, 1; totaling 355 shops. Among them, 94 shops closed due to sluggish business, 204 shops closed due to losses, 7 shops went bankrupt due to debt, and 50 shops closed for other reasons.

Hubei Province to Improve the Collection of Land Tax - Provincial Government Orders All Counties to Comply 104

Hankou Correspondence. Land tax is the main source of local revenue, and the administrative expenses of all provinces depend on it. The quota for land tax collection in Hubei Province is 1,893,200 yuan, which is less than that of other provinces. However, the actual amount collected each year is only about 30% to 40%. This not only affects the provincial treasury but also makes it difficult to maintain county administrative expenses. The reasons for the shortfall are mostly due to the disorganized collection registers, the difficulty in reversing the deep-rooted corruption, and the negligence of the collecting officials in thoroughly improving the situation. Yang Yongtai, the chairman of the provincial government, previously received a telegram from President Chiang ordering a thorough improvement. He has already drafted reform measures and issued a notice to all county magistrates on the 20th, outlining four points to be strictly followed: 1. Eliminate embezzlement. The clerks' control over collection and embezzlement of taxes for personal gain has been a common problem with land tax. County magistrates often follow the old ways and do not think of reform, resulting in deeper and deeper malpractices. In the future, they must check the tax collected daily, audit the accounts, and carefully select collection personnel in accordance with the repeated orders of this government, and strictly implement performance appraisal to clear up accumulated malpractices. 2. Sanction the powerful. Local powerful households own a large amount of land and often regard not paying taxes as an honor. The bad habits have been passed down and are almost regarded as exemptions. Some even harbor others, openly resisting and secretly rejecting the tax collection. Collecting officials are either intimidated by their power and have many concerns, or are hindered by friendship and turn a blind eye, which is extremely detrimental to tax administration. They should strictly comply with President Chiang's telegram to severely sanction them to warn the cunning and stubborn. 3. Strictly pursue old debts. The amount of arrears in land tax in each county is very large. The number of arrears in land tax over the years should be cleared up quickly, and methods for urging collection should be formulated, deadlines should be set, and arrears households should be ordered to pay. If they fail to pay after the deadline, they will be arrested and pursued, or their property will be confiscated to offset the arrears tax to enrich the treasury. 4. Rectify the new tax. In collecting the new tax, each county often neglects the busy season due to the uncleared old tax, leaving it to be overdue. Year after year, there is no hope of collecting the full amount according to the quota. It is extremely important to thoroughly rectify the situation, so that the people can pay on time and achieve the goal of collecting the full amount according to the quota. It is also said that the above four points are aimed at improving collection and eliminating old malpractices. However, the collection affairs are extremely trivial and must be diligently investigated from morning to night in order to achieve results. The county magistrates must not hand over the affairs to their subordinates due to the complexity of the affairs, so that the collection affairs will gradually decline. It is hoped that they will correct their previous mistakes and thoroughly improve the situation. After this decisive telegram, this government will regularly and strictly assess the amount of land tax collected in each county. If there is any more procrastination, negligence of tax administration, or short collection, which is less than the proportion, it will be severely punished and will never be tolerated. (20th)

A Perspective on Small Loan Offices in Nanjing - Loans Are Available to Those With Productive Capacity; More Than 350,000 Yuan Has Been Loaned Out 105

Nanjing Correspondence. The Nanjing Small Loan Office is an organization that is directly related to the common people. According to Yuan Shaoxian, the business director of the office, the situation of the office is very detailed. A brief record is as follows:

The driving force behind the establishment of the Nanjing Small Loan Office can be attributed to the Jin Cheng Bank. Zhou Zuomin, the general manager of the bank, believed that the existence of the bank must benefit the general society, but in essence, the common people rarely receive real benefits. Therefore, he volunteered to contribute 100,000 yuan. The Nanjing Municipal Government allocated 48,000 yuan, and the Capital Police Department allocated 2,000 yuan, making a total of 150,000 yuan as the loan fund for the office. It was established on December 3, 1934. The scope of the office's loans is limited to those who are engaged in small industrial and commercial businesses and lack capital. Therefore, only those who have productive capacity are given assistance. As for poor people who cannot make a living, such as beggars and disabled people, the office will absolutely not provide relief because this is a loan business, not a charitable business.

The nature of the loans is divided into seed loans, draught cattle loans, poor people's loans, and industrial and commercial loans. The first two types are all aimed at farmers. For seed loans, the procedures must be proven by the local township or rich farmers. It must be confirmed that there are several acres of land, and it must also be proven that the loan will indeed be used to purchase seeds and will not be used for other purposes. The amount of the loan ranges from a minimum of 40 cents to a maximum of about 10 yuan. A total of 4,166 households have borrowed 13,751.80 yuan. Draught cattle loans also require proof and a guarantee that the borrower will never sell the draught cattle. At the same time, after the loan is established, the loan office will brand the draught cattle as a mark. Even if it is sold in the future, it will be invalid once discovered. As of now, a total of 1,231 households have borrowed 23,220 yuan. The next is poor people's loans. The so-called poor people are those who have productive capacity but lack capital. The maximum limit is 5 yuan, with no interest, and must be repaid within five months. A total of 6,449 households have borrowed 3,178.00 yuan. Finally, there are industrial and commercial loans. These are aimed at those who are engaged in small industrial and commercial businesses. The amount of the loan ranges from 6 yuan to 200 yuan, and the interest is divided into four levels: 7% for 6 yuan to 20 yuan, 8% for 21 yuan to 50 yuan, 9% for 51 yuan to 100 yuan, and 1% for 101 yuan to 200 yuan. A total of 4,963 households have borrowed 285,045 yuan. In total, 16,810 households have borrowed 354,194.80 yuan, with an average loan of 21 yuan and 7 cents per household.

Regarding the loan procedures, the borrower must first fill out an application form, stating the amount of the loan, its purpose, the repayment period, etc., and submit it to the designated agent - the Autonomous Region Office - there are a total of eleven in the city. After a thorough investigation and evaluation, it is submitted to the office for approval. Then, the agent will notify the original borrower to complete the loan procedures, such as filling out a promissory note, having the guarantor stamp, etc. Finally, the money can be received in full. The repayment period is stipulated as one year, but if the borrower can repay in advance, they can do so at their convenience. There are several methods of repayment: fixed-term, installment, and flexible. The borrower can choose whichever method they prefer. A repayment statement is issued, stating the installment amount and the due date. The borrower goes to repay on time. In the past year, borrowers have been able to abide by their credit and rarely default. This is a great help to the promotion of the office's business and is worth mentioning.

What benefits can the existence of this office bring to the society? This is a question worth discussing. According to Mr. Yuan, at the end of the lunar year last year, about 30 to 40 stores in Xiaguan were on the verge of bankruptcy. Fortunately, they were helped by the office and were able to survive. According to the office's investigation, each borrower's household has an average of six or seven people, totaling more than 100,000 people. With a fund of 150,000 yuan, the amount of loans has reached more than 350,000 yuan. The number of beneficiaries is so large—accounting for one-tenth of the city's population—and on this point alone, the office has value in existing.

Large stores in Nanjing City, such as silk and satin shops, Western pharmacies, and restaurants, also frequently request loans from the office. The office staff once said, "You are large stores with tens of thousands or hundreds of thousands of capital. Why do you need to borrow money from a small loan office?" The answer is roughly this: Although the stores have a large capital, they have all used it to purchase goods, resulting in a lack of liquid cash and difficulty in turnover. The banks are unwilling to lend to the merchants. Because the stores are in urgent need of payment, they know that the small loan office cannot lend much, but being able to borrow 200 yuan can help them overcome the current difficulty. Finally, they also ask to keep it a secret because it relates to the store's reputation and face. If this news is leaked, it will inevitably suffer from the influence of squeeze and cause shake.

In addition, because of the need to purchase goods, they must raise a large sum of money, so they also come to the office to ask for help. What is the state of financial exhaustion in the Nanjing market? Here, we can get a very definite answer.

The office recently plans to increase its fund by 50,000 yuan due to the development of its business, bringing the total to 200,000 yuan. It is said that it will be realized soon. At that time, it can further increase the loan efficiency of the office to exert its greatest effect.

Suzhou: All Tofu Shops Raise Prices 106

There are no fewer than several hundred tofu shops in Suzhou, and they have an association as one of the members of the Chamber of Commerce. Recently, due to the impact of rising raw material prices, all the shops have felt it difficult to maintain their businesses. Therefore, they convened a general meeting of members on the 21st and resolved to raise the prices of all goods uniformly. It was also resolved that all businesses in the city would be closed for one day on the 22nd for reorganization. From the 23rd, the price increase will be implemented. The matter was reported to the party and government agencies for record and sent to the County Chamber of Commerce. After receiving the letter, the Chamber of Commerce stated that the reasons for the price increase were not clearly stated, and it was a matter related to the daily needs of the common people. Yesterday, it sent a letter to the association, urging them to carefully deliberate and make a decision before replying.

Wuxi: Bandits Rob Fishing Boats at Night 107

Recently, bandits have been rampant. Robberies and assaults are frequently heard in the four rural areas of the county. In the Lingyandang shoal area near Ganlu Town in the 8th district of the county, there is a man named Yin Qichang, who is over seventy years old, and his wife is also old. They both drive a small boat and make a living by fishing there. They are usually diligent and thrifty, so they have accumulated more than 700 yuan. Unexpectedly, they were targeted by bandits. At about 10 p.m. the other day, more than a dozen bandits suddenly rushed onto the boat, each holding iron rods and short knives, and tied up the Qichang couple, threatening them to make no noise. They searched arbitrarily, and more than 700 yuan in legal tender and foreign currency hidden in the bottom of the cabin were robbed. The hull of the boat was also damaged. The bandits then left with a roar. When it was dawn, they were discovered by others, and the Qichang couple was untied. However, the bandits had long since fled.

Purchased 80,000 Mulberry Seedlings 108

The Jiangsu Construction Department believes that the silkworm rearing results in various counties last year were excellent and the export of raw silk was active. It is expected that farmers will have a strong interest in silkworm rearing this year, and the orders for planting in various counties have increased sharply. The mulberry leaves will not be enough to distribute. Therefore, personnel were sent to Zhejiang to purchase more than 100,000 excellent mulberry seedlings. The silkworm mulberry model area of this county has received 80,000 branches and distributed them to various central guidance stations for silkworm farmers to purchase and plant. The cost of each branch is 1.3 cents. The amount needed for spring planting in the four rural areas of this county is expected to be more than 300,000 sheets. Currently, more than 172,500 sheets have been ordered, and 70,000 sheets of Japanese species ordered by the Jiangsu Provincial Silkworm Industry Management Committee have been transported to Wuxi. This county can allocate 30,000 sheets according to the previous year's plan.
