They were involved in the robbery and fatal stabbing of the monk Hanyan of the First Spring Temple, as well as the kidnapping and looting of Cao Songjie, the son of Cao Zhufu, a ferryman in Sanba. They also robbed Wang Shilan and Zhu Yaodong in Lingtang Township and fatally stabbed Wang Shilan. All of these cases have been clearly identified by the victims. The death penalty was approved by the Headquarters.

Yangzhou Rescued Student Escapes Danger from Abduction 114

Zhu Tinghua, the second son of Zhu Lüshi, a resident of the sixth troop tenth household of Sanbao Town, Shuangzhong County, Yangzhou (age thirteen), was studying at a private school across from the Dongquanmen Cloth Industry Guild. He suddenly disappeared on the 13th. Searches were fruitless. Unexpectedly, he returned home on the afternoon of the 18th. According to him, on the morning of the 13th, he was relieving himself in a small outhouse made of a charcoal basket when a strong man wearing a fur coat over a gray mandarin jacket suddenly appeared and knocked him down. He lost consciousness and only knew that he was running with the man. They went out of the city and boarded a boat where he was confined to the bottom of the hold, which was weighted down with large stones. He was taken to Zhenjiang, and given only two pieces of bread per day. When he needed to relieve himself, the boat would go into the middle of the river. The next day, he heard crying from the rear hold, realizing another child had been brought. The child was calling for his mother and was beaten severely. After noon on the 18th, all was silent. He secretly investigated and found no one around. He struggled with all his might and overturned the stones, escaping the hold and freeing the child from the rear hold. He learned that the child had been abducted from Nanjing, his father was a battalion commander, and he had an aunt in town. His own small fur coat had been taken from him. They decided to flee together. They saw a rope tied to the bow of the boat, very far from the shore. He braved the danger and climbed the rope to shore. The other child went to find his aunt, while he ran to the steamship bureau, recounted his abduction, and received a free ticket, enabling him to return to Yangzhou.

The Jiangdu County Government, upon receiving an order from the Department of Finance, will inspect the cash holdings of various government agencies. Originally scheduled for the 25th, it has been moved to the 22nd because the Chief Accountant and the Chief of the Second Section must go to the provincial capital on the 24th to await examination and will not be able to return to the county by the 25th. The inspection of various agencies will be moved to the 22nd, and a report will be submitted to the Department of Finance for record.

Nantong Girl Killed by Father Sentenced to Five Years 116

Yao Fu, a resident of Nanxiang Township, Liuqiao District, Nantong, because his wife Chen gave birth to a girl instead of a boy, actually killed the newborn baby by throwing her to the ground. The neighbors were outraged and reported him to the court. The prosecutor sent police to exhume the baby's body for examination, confirming the cause of death. Yao Fu was detained for interrogation and then imprisoned. On the 20th, the Criminal Court concluded the trial and sentenced him to five years in prison. Yao Fu accepted the sentence and was sent to prison.

Adulterous Daughter-in-Law Murders Mother-in-Law, Prosecutor Seeks Death Penalty 117

Gu Wangshi, a young woman from Yu Dong, Nantong, was having an affair with her cousin, Gu Haitao, who lived with her. When her mother-in-law discovered the affair, they were enraged and, in the night, the adulterous couple stabbed the mother-in-law to death and buried her body in the field to cover up the crime. The district office discovered the crime, arrested the two criminals, and handed them over to the court. On the 20th, Prosecutor Wang indicted Gu Wangshi and Gu Haitao with the death penalty.

Kunshan Awards for Efforts in Curing Rice Stem Borers 118

Last year, rice stem borers ravaged this county, causing severe damage. The autumn harvest was greatly reduced. County Magistrate Peng Baichuan, in order to prevent future problems, specially invited agricultural experts from various places to formulate effective measures to eliminate rice stem borers. A general mobilization was launched in October and completed in mid-December. It is now known that County Magistrate Peng will reward those who worked hard to cure the rice stem borers, including five people who will receive commendations, seventeen district and township chiefs who will receive certificates of merit, six people who will receive citations, and four farmers who will be rewarded. It quickly spread to the Tongrenyuan Grocery Store across the street, as well as the adjacent Zheng Shenyuan Nanhua Store (already closed), Tianhe Rice Store, Chunmao Bamboo Shoot Store, Yuanfengtai Noodle Pot Store, Wanshengtang Pharmacy, Han family wall door Chunbao Fruit Stall, Hu Desheng water workshop, Yuanfeng Meat Store, Shunxing Meat Store, Wang Wanxing Pastry Store, and sixteen households including the Xu family. Bengbu Strange Twins 122

In Yangqiao, southeast of Sixian County, Northern Anhui, there is a farmer named Liu Zhongxin, approaching the age of thirty. His wife, He, is of similar age. Last year, she became pregnant and her abdomen was particularly large. Recently, she gave birth to two children, a boy and a girl, which are slightly different from ordinary twins. The boy's body is short and small, his head is flat and large, shaped like an inverted bowl, with a thin skin on top that hangs down around the edges, about two inches long, covering his forehead and eyes. When lifted by hand, both eyes are fully visible. When released, the eyes cannot see. The girl has all the usual facial features and her body is normal, except that both hands have fused fingers, shaped like a Zen staff, without distinction between size or length. The toes on both feet are also the same. After birth, she nurses like a normal child. However, their strange forms are rare among twins, and everyone clicks their tongues in amazement. This is recorded for research purposes.

Page 12

Local News

Minister of Finance Proposes, Striving for Production and Construction Plan, Approved by the Central Political Council and Submitted to the Executive Yuan for Distribution to Various Ministries for Implementation Measures to be Submitted Within One Month 123

A special dispatch from Xin Xin News Agency reports that at the beginning of his tenure, Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi convened a financial meeting to discuss major policy issues, such as abolishing excessive taxes and miscellaneous levies, reducing and exempting surcharges on land taxes to benefit the people's livelihood, implementing a balanced tax to prevent the outflow of silver, and implementing the legal tender policy. He advocated the path of self-reliance to adjust finances and revive the nation. His painstaking efforts, determination, and far-sighted vision have long been recognized by the people of the country. The "Striving for Construction" proposal he put forward at the Sixth Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee, including plans for various avenues to develop people's livelihood and strive for construction, was extremely comprehensive. It is reported that the case has been discussed and resolved by the Eighth Meeting of the Central Political Committee, passed according to the review opinions of the Economic Expert Committee, and submitted to the Executive Yuan for distribution to the Ministries of Interior, Industry, Finance, Railways, Communications, Foreign Affairs, and Education, with a deadline of one month for submitting implementation measures. A reporter from Xin Xin News Agency specially excerpted the original proposal as follows:

Strive for Self-Salvation

I believe that the path to saving the country has countless aspects, but the fundamental point lies entirely in the government and the people striving for self-salvation. Since the establishment of the National Government, we have followed the teachings of Sun Yat-sen and worked hard to unify internally. After years of hard work, banditry has gradually been suppressed. When the banditry was at its height, the country was in turmoil, almost unmanageable. Thanks to the military and political authorities and the people of the whole country unanimously resisting with perseverance, the work of stabilization was finally achieved. This is a clear and great verification of self-salvation, which we can take comfort in.

Implement Economic Self-Sufficiency

In recent years, floods and droughts have occurred frequently, leaving scars everywhere. The national rural areas are declining, and industry and commerce are shrinking. Domestic production is decreasing daily, and the huge trade deficit reaches 700 to 800 million yuan annually. Not only are industrial products dependent on foreigners, but even the required food cannot be self-sufficient. Economic collapse is imminent. The demise of the country can be expected at any moment. The plan for today is to thoroughly awaken, vigorously rejuvenate, and pledge to implement the policy of economic self-sufficiency with the spirit of national self-salvation. Gather the financial and human resources of the people of the whole country, concentrate them on economic construction, base them on a definite plan, and succeed in completing the plan within a set period.

Government Establishes Definite Plans

Our country has vast land and abundant resources. Its natural productivity is no less than that of European and American countries. The key to utilizing natural forces to seek advancement in production lies in diligent perseverance, strong will, and astute planning. The key is to not rely on others but to focus on self-reliance. Soviet Russia and Italy are even more barren than our country, but one implements a five-year plan and the other promotes a self-sufficiency policy. Both rely on the diligence and self-improvement of their people, tightening their belts, and focusing on production, finally leading their countries to prosperity. Japan is a small country with poor people, but through the hard work and struggle of its people, it has also been able to establish itself as an industrial and commercial nation and dominate the world. Although these countries use different methods, they all succeeded through self-salvation. Our country is in the midst of fierce global economic competition. The government should establish a production and construction plan, supervise and encourage the people to advance rapidly, so that the situation of collapse can be reversed.

Principles of Production and Construction

Production and construction have many aspects, but the phrase "utilize the land to its fullest, utilize people to their fullest, and utilize resources to their fullest" can encompass everything without omission. "Utilizing the land to its fullest" means not only making fertile soil and land suitable for planting to fully utilize its benefits, but also finding ways to improve and trial-plant barren and saline areas that everyone considers abandoned land, to achieve the goal of increasing production. "Utilizing people to their fullest" means not only allowing those with skills to each find their place, and giving idle people jobs, so that there is not a single person in the country who lives without working, but also using one person to do the work of two, and completing the work of two days in one day, so that consumption is reduced and production is increased, achieving the greatest effect at the lowest cost. "Utilizing resources to their fullest" means not only making sure that the treasures of mountains and seas are not abandoned, and that bamboo heads and wood chips are all suitable for use, but also transferring useless uses to useful uses, and transferring uses with less profit to uses with more profit, so that the power of production becomes more expansive, and its benefits become more widespread. The above are the principles of production and construction. The detailed outline of methods is summarized below:

Emphasize Production Education

Primary and secondary education is the foundation of education and is of great importance to people's lives and the survival of the country. Now that we are striving for production and construction, the direction of education should naturally be aimed at production. All primary and secondary school courses should focus on teaching students knowledge and skills related to production, and provide them with ample opportunities for practice, so that after leaving school, they can independently earn a living, directly increase production efficiency, and indirectly cultivate people's habits of self-reliance.

Concentrate People's Power

Our country has always emphasized etiquette and culture. Daily social interactions and funeral ceremonies cost a lot, consume useful money, and cultivate wasteful habits. It is appropriate to improve them. It is proposed to stipulate restrictions on various ceremonies such as weddings, birthdays, funerals, and sacrifices, and on gifts and banquets, specifying standards and not allowing abuse. Violators will be punished. Efforts should also be made to promote thrift and savings, so that they can be used for production undertakings. Furthermore, our country's temples and ancestral halls own a lot of property, most of which is used for consumption. This not only hinders production but also fosters a culture of living without working among the people. It should be stipulated by law that all folk temple and ancestral hall properties should be utilized as much as possible, with a portion used to run production undertakings and a portion transferred to support old age, care for orphans, and educational public welfare purposes. Local governments should strictly investigate and provide appropriate rewards and encouragement. It is proposed that the Ministries of Interior and Finance review the measures for implementation.

Guarantee Bank Credit

Since the global economic panic, financial tightening in various countries has greatly affected all industries. Even the United States, with its vast capital, implemented emergency measures, and the government's assistance to banks gradually led to stability. Our country's banks have weak capital and unsound organizations, and industrial and commercial enterprises urgently need access to funds to develop. If the government does not strongly support the banks, allowing them to invest in various industries with peace of mind, they will collapse immediately if they encounter risks. In the future, it is planned that the government will provide appropriate guarantees for the legitimate use and safekeeping of funds of various banks, and instruct them to provide low-interest loans to agricultural and industrial enterprises. The government will provide appropriate subsidies for the loss of interest. In this way, the financial foundation can be consolidated, and the development of industries can be expected.

Promote Labor-Management Cooperation

In industrialized countries, labor and management have become separate classes, and the struggle between them is fierce, which is detrimental to both. Our country follows Sun Yat-sen's teachings and establishes the country on the basis of the Three Principles of the People, so there should be no class struggle. However, factories are now in their infancy, and labor unions are gradually developing. In order to prevent labor disputes and maintain the healthy development of industry, the government should adopt a labor-management coordination policy, protecting both labor and management without partiality. Employers should provide employees with appropriate wages and adequate facilities, and employees should work diligently for employers to increase production efficiency. The two sides should understand and assist each other, each doing their best, and production can be increased, and costs can be reduced. This will not only promote international trade but also invisibly eliminate labor-management disputes. Therefore, all laws and regulations regarding working hours and wage standards that are not appropriate in the current laws and regulations should be revised to be feasible. At the same time, attention should also be paid to labor arbitration, labor insurance, vocational education, and labor-management consumer cooperation. It is proposed that the Ministry of Industry carefully discuss and implement these matters.

Advocate Running Heavy Industry

Heavy industry is the mother of all industries, and its importance is almost above all other industries. In the Material Construction section of Sun Yat-sen's The International Development of China, Sun proposed that counties establish factories to manufacture agricultural implements, etc., with the intention of being thorough. Furthermore, in the Soviet Union's first five-year plan, full efforts were devoted to the establishment of the machinery industry, placing light industry in a supporting position, so that it was able to establish an industrial foundation, and production consequently increased rapidly. Our country's light industry has been in its infancy recently, but the required machinery and metal raw materials are mostly purchased from foreign countries, and the industry has lost its independence, resulting in being controlled by foreigners, and the future is worrying. Therefore, for the sake of industrial development, special attention should also be paid to China. On the one hand, the state should operate selective industries, and on the other hand, it should encourage people to invest in and run industries. Existing private heavy industries with achievements should be helped to expand. Perhaps in five or ten years, production tools can be self-sufficient. The Ministry of Industry is requested to determine the methods and proceed as soon as possible.

Promote Industrial Rationalization

Domestic industries have shown slight progress in recent years, but mostly due to improper management, poor technology, or other shortcomings, the cost is too high to compete with foreign goods, and many have been closed down. The competent authorities should investigate domestic factories and carefully assess them. If any of the above circumstances exist, they should be ordered to improve, or managed on their behalf, or ordered to reorganize thoroughly, so that they tend to rationalize, so as to reduce costs and increase production, to support national production and facilitate sales. The detailed plan is requested to be carefully drafted by the Ministry of Industry and submitted for implementation.

Promote Cottage Industry

Our country has attached importance to both men farming and women weaving since ancient times. For example, most of the domestic coarse cloth is produced by women's spinning and weaving. Since the import of foreign yarn, this industry has been abandoned, and women at home are sitting idle and doing nothing, learning to be extravagant, only knowing how to consume and not produce. Even in various places, there are businesses engaged in making hairnets, lace, and embroidery, and selling their products abroad, the scope is very narrow, and most of them are controlled by foreigners, and the results are still small. It seems appropriate to promptly formulate measures to encourage cottage industries and supervise people to organize cottage industry cooperatives to operate jointly to achieve great results. In this way, unemployed men and women at home can all use small industries to support themselves, which increases production power and fosters a habit of thrift. It is proposed that the Ministries of Industry and Interior review the implementation measures.

Utilize Waste Land

According to expert statistics, China has no less than 4 billion mu of arable land, but only 1.5 billion mu are currently cultivated. There is idle land and people, and production is shrinking, resulting in the need to rely on foreigners for daily food and industrial raw materials. The plan for today is to not only improve the cultivated land as much as possible to increase production, but also to investigate the wasteland and supervise its utilization. If it belongs to private individuals and is not reclaimed within three years, or if it is not effective within five years, it should be confiscated by the state. If it belongs to the state, a wasteland reclamation agency should be jointly established by the central and local governments to engage in land reclamation, or to conscript migrant workers and incorporate them into soldiers to provide service. Even for barren land that is not suitable for cultivation, it is appropriate to learn from Italy's example of opening up mountain gaps and planting grapes for winemaking, selecting varieties according to local conditions, and planting them separately. The detailed plan is requested

International Trade Balance

to be jointly drafted by the Ministries of Industry and Finance. Over the years, our country has had a large trade deficit. If the leaks are not stopped, there is no way to survive. The plan for today is to find ways to balance international trade as soon as possible. The government can directly or indirectly manage import trade. The implementation steps should be based on the trade situation in various countries, and carefully discuss barter trade or import and export ratio methods, and change the International Trade Bureau to be under the jurisdiction of the Ministries of Finance and Industry to complete the above tasks. For export goods, standards should also be specified in accordance with business conditions to seek uniformity and facilitate sales. The Ministries of Industry and Finance are requested to carefully draft plans and proceed as soon as possible.

Unify State-Owned Enterprises

Production undertakings value concentration, which not only achieves greater results but also saves costs. Given our country's weak financial resources and lack of talent, if various construction undertakings are organized with divergent functions and powers, the plans will not be well-considered, and costs will also increase, inevitably resulting in being twice the effort for half the results. All unnecessary and redundant equipment should be abolished, and redundant institutions should be eliminated to reduce expenditure and increase work efficiency. The government is requested to convene various competent authorities to discuss thoroughly and decide on practical measures for implementation.

Adopt the Labor Conscription System

The levy of labor in our country has always been parallel to the tax system. Originally, public undertakings needed labor, and the people could contribute their surplus strength to help the country, which was a very good intention. Now that we are engaged in various construction projects, a lot of labor is needed. Rather than increasing micro-taxes and burdens, it is better to promote the labor conscription method. However, those who cannot personally participate in the work should pay money instead to show fairness. It is proposed to stipulate that able-bodied men in the country, from the age of twenty to fifty-five, should fulfill their obligation to work for three days each year for national and local construction undertakings, during the agricultural off-season. Those who have fixed occupations and incomes and have no time to serve should pay money according to three days' wages, which will be allocated for the specified purposes. All undertakings and public benefits related to central and local public welfare, or for public use by the people, may be subject to the micro-labor method. As for how to conscript and distribute the work, the Ministry of Interior is requested to draft an outline, and the various localities will formulate detailed rules for submission and implementation. If this is appropriate, we respectfully await public decision. Proposers: Kong Xiangxi, Huang Jilu, Jiao Yitang, Chuan Rulin, Qin Zhen, Liang Hancao.

Change of British Ambassador to China, Foreign Newspapers Discuss Political Observers 127

The Da Mei Evening Post reports that political observers in Shanghai believe that the sudden announcement of the replacement of British Ambassador to China Sir Knatchbull-Hugessen by Sir Archibald Clark Kerr comes at a time when the new Japanese Ambassador to China, Akira Ariyoshi, is about to take office. They see a connection, believing that the changes of the British and Japanese ambassadors are clear signs of slight changes in the two countries' policies towards China. It is now believed that Britain's policy will be firmer than before, while Japan's policy, partly due to London's stance in recent months, will not be as focused on active expansion as before. Sources in Japanese circles claim that Ariyoshi's arrival in China will involve discussions with China to resolve accumulated cases between the two countries over the past five years. Many observers believe that if this resolution is successful, the new situation created by Japan's use of force since the September 18th Incident will be greatly strengthened. However, at the same time, Japan's progressive active expansion in mainland China will cease. These sources also believe that since Sir Frederick Leith-Ross came to China, Britain's policy has been to contain Japan's expansion. Recently, many reports have been published stating that although Sir Frederick Leith-Ross's trip appeared to be only for economic investigation, his trip was opposed by the British Foreign Office, and British Ambassador Sir Knatchbull-Hugessen did not welcome him much either. However, after a major change in the British Foreign Office, Sir Frederick Leith-Ross achieved great success in the currency reform in Nanjing and the relaxation of Japan's autocratic actions in North China, and was thus trusted by the British government and public. Furthermore, the new British Ambassador to China, Sir Archibald Clark Kerr, recently served as Minister to Iran (Persia). In recent years, Britain has pursued a very firm policy in that country to resist Soviet Russia's encroachment on Iran. Therefore, Kerr's transfer to China is also related. Sir Frederick Leith-Ross is currently in Guangzhou and is scheduled to return to Shanghai next week. According to a guest in Hong Kong who spoke with Sir Leith-Ross, the Chinese currency system is now gradually improving, China is currently not negotiating international loans, and he strongly supports the connection between the Guangdong-Hankou Railway and the Kowloon-Canton Railway, so that goods from the Chinese mainland can be transported to Hong Kong.

Ambassador Gu Admitted to Hospital for Treatment Yesterday; Condition Gradually Improving, Recovery Requires Time, Discharge Date Still Difficult to Predict 129

Therefore, on the morning of the 21st, he was sent to the Hong'en Hospital on Great West Road by his wife and others for treatment. It is still difficult to predict when he will be discharged from the hospital. Second Freeze-Up Outside Dagukou; More Than Twenty Ships Trapped in Ice; Situation More Severe Than the First Time 132

The severe cold in North China this year is unprecedented in over a century. It has been one and a half months since Dagukou froze over. On the 7th of this month, the Taikoo Line's S.S. New Shengjing used a special icebreaker to rescue the company's S.S. Nanchang, S.S. Huizhou, and other ships, breaking through four feet of solid ice for eighty-one nautical miles, allowing navigation for several days. Unexpectedly, since the 17th, strong southwest winds have risen for days, and the weather has been unusually cold. Ice floes have blown to the sea outside Dagukou again, re-freezing the previously opened航路, which is even more serious than the first time.

Ships Trapped

The Taikoo Line's S.S. Ganzhou has been surrounded by solid ice and has run aground on the ice bank with a damaged rudder. It is awaiting rescue. The S.S. Yingzhou is also on the ice, moving back and forth with the ice tide, drifting on the sea. The S.S. New Shengjing, which loaded cargo and passengers in Shanghai this time, arrived outside Dagukou on the afternoon of the 18th. The icebreaker was also ineffective and unable to resist the ice tide, so it had to turn back to Yantai midway. The Jardine Matheson's S.S. Rising Sun, which departed from Tianjin, also turned back to Tanggu to dock. In total, there are twenty-five ships from China, Britain, Japan, Norway, and other countries that have been blocked by ice again.

Passengers in Distress

Passengers trapped in the ice have no food or drink, causing great panic. Fortunately, the special icebreaker "巧利摩勒" (Chiao Li Mo Le) sent by Tianjin, together with rescue boats, gradually broke the ice and reached the ice sea, rescuing seventy passengers from the S.S. Shunli and one hundred passengers from the S.S. Chosen Maru to Dagukou. However, due to the ice freezing as soon as it was broken, no ship has been able to escape the danger, and it is now impossible to rescue the passengers trapped in the ice. Individual shipping companies telegraphed the Tianjin Harbor Bureau yesterday, requesting that a powerful icebreaker be sent to rescue them as soon as possible, otherwise the crew and passengers would face the worry of running out of food.

Foreign Media Reports

According to the Da Mei Evening News, the Shanghai Xujiahui Observatory reported that the weather along the Chinese coast today (the 21st) remains bad, and navigation is greatly affected. Strong northerly winds with speeds of 25 to 30 miles per hour are currently hindering the navigation of ships between Shanghai and Hong Kong. There was drizzle at the southern ports at 6:00 AM, and visibility was still poor. Therefore, the three British airships that wanted to fly to Shanghai have temporarily postponed their departure. It is currently snowing in Tianjin and Tanggu in the north, and the temperature has dropped below freezing, so about twenty-five ships are reported to be frozen in the Bohai Bay. There is currently no hope of them sailing out.

Joint Reserve Committee of Banks Establishes Bank Acceptance House; Articles of Association Approved and to be Established in Short Term; Aim is to Revive Commerce and Industry and Restore the Market 133

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, the Shanghai Banking Association Joint Reserve Committee's proposal to establish a Bank Acceptance House has been approved by the representatives of the member banks and will be established in the short term. The details are as follows:

Establishment of Acceptance House

The Bank Acceptance House will be affiliated with the Banking Association Joint Reserve Committee, and its nature will be the same as that of the bank clearing house. The articles of association have been approved, and the fifth executive committee of the committee, consisting of Li Fusun, Bei Songsun, Tang Shoumin, Xu Jilao, Qian Xinzhi, Chen Guangfu, Chen Zheqing, and others, together with manager Zhu Boquan, deputy manager Xu Baoqi, and assistant managers Kong Bao-cheng and Ye Chunquan, are preparing for its establishment. The address has been decided to be within the committee on Hong Kong Road, and it is expected to be established in the short term.

Reviving Commerce and Industry

The acceptance method involves designating domestic commercial firms to use valuable goods stored in bank warehouses as collateral. After bank acceptance is approved and signed, it can be circulated and traded on the market or discounted at the committee's banks. At the same time, banks that accept discounts can rediscount with other banks or rediscount with leading banks when they need funds. This type of bank acceptance bill has excellent credit and can increase market liquidity, allowing industry and commerce to obtain financing. It will be beneficial to the entire market and can be controlled.

Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers' Association to Discuss Telephone Issues This Afternoon; Report on Telephone Issues to be Released 137

The Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers' Association is scheduled to convene an executive committee meeting at 4:00 PM today (22nd) to discuss the issue of telephone charges in the Special District. The association also released a report yesterday on the issue of telephone rates in the Special District for reference by those who are concerned about this issue. The original report is as follows:

After the Shanghai Telephone Company completed the automatic telephone system (the extra-settlement roads have not been completed), it applied to the Public Works Department of the International Settlement to increase prices according to the contract. Users protested, and as a result, the price increased by 25%. Residential phones increased from 52 to 65 taels of silver, and commercial phones increased from 78 to 105 taels of silver. Although the increase started on July 1, 1932, it was retroactive to March 27 of that year because that was the date the renovation was completed. Furthermore, the usage fee was changed from a quarterly payment to a monthly payment. Users protested most strongly, and some had their phones removed. The rest paid the increased price under protest. Although the association actively argued on the basis of reason, it was ineffective. In October 1933, the Shanghai Telephone Company requested another price increase, intending to increase the price by another one-fifth, that is, residential phones would be charged 81 taels, 2 mace, and 5 candareens, and commercial phones would be charged 131 taels, 2 mace, and 5 candareens. The association sent a letter to the Public Works Department, expressing extreme opposition. The Public Works Department stated that the contract did not allow for a price increase within three years, so this price increase was not implemented. In 1935, the Shanghai Telephone Company stated that its profits were only 6% dividends and had not reached the 8% dividends and 2% reserves allowed by the contract, and it again applied to the Public Works Department for a price increase, intending to slightly increase residential phones and change commercial phones to pay-per-call. Users protested even more strongly. Therefore, at the representatives' meeting of the Ratepayers' Association on April 16, it was resolved to "urge the Public Works Department to organize a committee of experts to review the accounts of the Shanghai Telephone Company" and to issue a declaration: "The representatives' meeting believes that increasing telephone prices during this period of commercial recession is absolutely impossible. As for pay-per-call, there are many drawbacks and it is even more difficult to agree to. Furthermore, the service of the telephone company is not as good as the Shanghai Telephone Bureau, and the charges are higher. There are also many areas where internal expenses can be reduced. The association advocates that the Public Works Department should hire Chinese and foreign experts and representatives of the Chinese users with the most users to form a committee to thoroughly and comprehensively review the company's situation and strive to reduce unnecessary expenses and increase service efficiency to meet the purpose of public utilities," expressing opposition. This is the concept obtained before the establishment of the expert committee, and it is a unanimous resolution. On April 17, the meeting of Western ratepayers resolved, "In view of the fact that ratepayers have not yet had sufficient opportunities to study the proposed telephone price increase plan of the Shanghai Telephone Company, and in view of the unprecedentedly sluggish state of Shanghai's commerce and economy, we, the ratepayers, hereby request the Public Works Department to conduct negotiations with the company so as to postpone the immediate price increase and to have time to consult a special telephone committee. The committee should consist of one or more experts who are familiar with telephone technology and business and have no connection with public utility companies in Shanghai. The committee should be formed by the Public Works Department in consultation with several organizations in the Shanghai International Settlement that are most representative of residents of all nationalities." This motion was proposed by Mr. Qian Wei Jing, a Japanese national, and seconded by Mr. Qian Nong Yisan Lang, proving that the Japanese nationals opposed the most among the foreigners. However, after this resolution, the Public Works Department temporarily approved the telephone company to increase the price by 11% from April 1. The Public Works Department followed the above motion and hired British expert Mr. Braun, followed by Mr. Hu Ruixiang (Director of the Long-Distance Telephone Office of the Ministry of Communications) and Mr. Inada, who were added due to the dispute between the association and the Japanese nationals. Mr. Lei was added again due to company relations. The terms of reference of the Special Committee of Telephone Experts set by the Public Works Department are as follows: "1. Consider whether the Shanghai Telephone Company has the right to increase telephone prices from April 1, 1935, in accordance with the provisions of the franchise contract. Whether the expenditure on all equipment, various mechanical devices, and other industries required for business is economically sound, and whether the current operating and maintenance costs of the company are economically reasonable, and submit to the Public Works Department on the construction of the above items. 2. Consider whether it is appropriate to use a fixed-charge method for commercial phones, home phones, or both. If it is deemed appropriate, prepare a tariff for the fixed-charge method so that the operating capital invested by the company can obtain the net profit stipulated in the franchise contract, and submit to the Public Works Department on the above items. 3. Consider that if the per-call charge is still used, (A) commercial phone fee, (B) home phone fee, and (C) other fees included in the tariff, such as should be increased, how much should each be increased so that the operating capital invested by the company can exclusively obtain the net profit stipulated in the franchise contract, and submit to the Public Works Department on the above items." The association saw that its scope was too narrow, so it proposed to the Public Works Department to expand the scope, with three reasons: "1. The object of study should be the entire company, so the scope of study of this case should be the entire Shanghai Telephone Company. 2. The largest expenditures of the Shanghai Telephone Company should be the annual interest of 10% for shareholders and reserves, the operating income subsidy of 4.5% obtained by the International Electric Material Company, and the purchase material commission of 5%, and the income tax paid by the company. 3. If the Shanghai Telephone Company does not use the 'Haiqin' method when purchasing materials to avoid changes in exchange rates, then the losses caused by the changes must be huge." The three areas that should be expanded are as follows: "1. The guaranteed interest rate of the world's telephone business is far from the guaranteed interest rate of the Shanghai Telephone Company here, and the 6% company bonds of the Shanghai Telephone Company are issued in Shanghai and there is no excess. Is the guaranteed interest rate of 8% dividends and 2% reserves, totaling 10%, reasonable? We propose its reasonable interest rate. 2. Should the operating income subsidy, purchase material commission, and income tax be outside the operating expenses? 3. Is there a way to avoid the losses caused by exchange rate changes? To whom does the fault belong? Should it be compensated by the public?" The association also sent the letter to various organizations such as the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, requesting their attention. Furthermore, since the Public Works Department did not adopt the three proposed expanded areas, it sent a letter to the Bureau solemnly stating, "If the scope of this study is not expanded, then the study report, the association will not be able to recognize it as satisfying the wishes of telephone users. There is room for consideration on this issue." Later, the Public Works Department replied, stating that the first issue of guaranteed interest was stipulated in the contract. The establishment of the expert committee was not to discuss the validity of the contract, but to consider how to fulfill the provisions of the contract under the current situation. The second issue of operating subsidies and purchase commissions had already been agreed upon by both parties to be discussed later. As for the third issue, the Bureau's proposed scope already included the provision to study the economic soundness of the telephone company's expenses. At the same time, an opinion was also submitted to the expert committee. According to the expert committee's report, 1. Regarding the telephone company's right to increase prices, it is considered a legal interpretation and does not express any opinion, but it is believed that there is a right. 2. Regarding the expenditure on equipment, devices, and industries of the telephone company, it is considered to be economically sound. 3. Regarding the operating and maintenance expenses of the telephone company, it is considered satisfactory, but there are several items that still need to be reduced. 4. Regarding the charging method, it is considered that a fixed-charge method should be adopted, regardless of residential or commercial use. 5. Regarding the price, it is proposed that commercial telephones be charged 10 yuan per month for 150 calls, and residential telephones be charged 6 yuan and 5 jiao per month for 100 calls. Beyond this limit, each call will be charged an additional 3 fen. The most important point that cannot be ignored is that although the charge is based on a fixed number of calls, the committee did not advocate, "There is a time limit for each call." As for other prices, some have been reduced, but most have increased, and the increase is very large. The expert committee's initial thought on the price for those who still use the per-call charge was that if a new price for the per-call charge method was charged in Shanghai, it would definitely reduce the number of users. The original report did not propose it. It was said in the supplement report that the per-call price should be 15 yuan and 5 jiao per month for commercial use and 9 yuan and 2 jiao and 5 fen per month for residential use. The current fixed-charge user pays 11 yuan per month for 150 calls, and additional calls are charged accordingly. However, the committee concluded, "The per-call charging method is not only not advocated by the committee, but it is resolutely considered unsuitable." After the release of the report of the Special Committee of Telephone Experts, the public opinion trend had generally tended to consider the fixed-charge method as reasonable in principle, so there were the following arguments: 1. Reduce the basic fee. 2. Increase the number of original limited calls. 3. Reduce the price of calls beyond the limit. According to the investigation, the current price and limit were debated fiercely in the committee. It was only due to the efforts of Committee Member Hu that this result was achieved. According to the Public Works Department's public bulletin, the following paragraph is included in the Board of Directors' minutes regarding the adoption of the report: "The Director-General also said that this morning (November 11, 1935), he met with a certain director who represented the Chinese directors and asked him to negotiate the following points with the telephone company: 1. Revise the fixed-charge tariff recommended by the telephone experts (i.e., commercial phone fee of 10 silver yuan per month for 150 calls, and home phone fee of 6 silver yuan and 5 jiao per month for 100 calls) as follows: Commercial phone fee of 10 silver yuan per month for 200 calls, and home phone fee of 6 silver yuan and 5 jiao per month for 150 calls. 2. The revised tariff shall be implemented from April 1, 1936 (i.e., one year after the temporary 11% price increase method is implemented) (the temporary price increase method was implemented from April 1, 1935). 3. After the above-mentioned revised tariff is adopted, the Bureau should immediately ask the company to revise the tariff at any time if the company's investment income exceeds the permitted 10% so that the telephone fee is immediately reduced. If the above-mentioned revised tariff is in place, the company shall not request another price increase within five years from the date of implementation of the tariff. 4. The Bureau should ask the company to further reduce operating and maintenance costs." According to the Director-General's discussion with the telephone company, the company did not agree to the first item. The company was willing to accept the second item, but changed April 1 to March 1. Regarding the third item, the company was also willing to accept the first point, but could not agree to the second point that there should be no price increase within five years. The company accepted the fourth item. After deliberation, there was no room for maneuver on the International Settlement's side. On the side of the French Concession's Public Works Bureau, although the Ratepayers' Association of that Concession proposed revisions, it was handled in accordance with the Public Works Department of the International Settlement. The major reason for this case is naturally that the guaranteed interest rate allowed by the franchise contract is too high, but once the contract is signed, the Public Works Department naturally has no way to break it. After the new method is implemented, it is a matter of fact whether the income of the telephone company is reduced by many removals and the company still cannot obtain the permitted interest. However, legally, if the telephone company still cannot get its wish, the Public Works Department will naturally have to approve it if the telephone company applies for a price increase. The failure of the Sino-Foreign Telephone Company was based on this. If the effectiveness and cost are not consistent, in other words, if the effectiveness is low and the cost is high, the demand will naturally decrease. The Director-General of the Public Works Department used the analogy of water meters, but he did not carefully consider that telephone and tap water are economically completely different in nature, because the former is something that can be freely chosen, while the latter is indispensable for life. Now, the opposition's strategy is to prefer removal rather than achieve their goal, but there have been two waves of telephone price increases. The first time was during the Sino-Foreign Telephone Company era, when both commercial and residential phones had to pay per call, limited to 300 calls. As a result of the opposition, the per-call charge was still used, but the price increase was very large, and many people voluntarily removed their phones. The second time was the price increase in 1932, when many people also voluntarily removed their phones, but it was not enough to make the telephone company stop the price increase. The extent to which users need telephones varies greatly, and there is no centralized union, so judging from the facts, the method of removal has historical evidence and is difficult to be effective. Then what will be the result of relying on nature? It can be predicted that the market will become more depressed, and some public agencies with the most economic foundation will also greatly reduce staff. Therefore, for telephones, which are still considered dispensable in our country, the demand for them will inevitably decrease due to the recession in the market. However, for users who need telephones the most, their business is mostly contacted on the telephone, and their expenses will inevitably increase greatly. Some have two telephones, and the average calculation is that each phone requires 40 calls per day. Some brokers calculate that one telephone has as many as 200 calls per day. Finally, it must be noted that although it was mentioned above that there is no time limit for each call, according to reports, the telephone company stipulates in the new regulations that hotels, associations, etc. are limited to five minutes for each call, and every five minutes beyond this will be counted as one call. If it is less than five minutes, it will also be counted as one call. The Public Works Department ordered that it not be implemented, but this article was not removed from the regulations. I do not know the reason for this. This must be solemnly reported. February 22, 1936.

Nanyang Commercial Inspection Delegation: Qualification of Participating Members Announced Yesterday by the Delegation 140

The Nanyang Commercial Inspection Delegation of this city, scheduled to depart in May, is approaching its departure date. Various factory members are enthusiastically participating. However, there are three types of members. Factory members should pay close attention when participating. The delegation announced the qualifications for participation yesterday morning as follows: Factories that believe their products can gain sales in Nanyang and can supply the necessary funding and personnel can participate as Class A members. Factories that are not fully confident in promoting their products or cannot supply the necessary funding and personnel can consult with employee factories in similar industries, discuss with several factories, and each send one person, or register temporarily with the Association. When members of the same type register, they can consult with each other and jointly send personnel. Factories that cannot send personnel but want to bring samples for exhibition and promotion or introduce sales can participate as Class C members and entrust the Association as an agent. The detailed rules for the agency will be determined separately. Member factories wishing to join the delegation must fill out a volunteer form, stating which type of member they wish to join, and prepay the allocated public funds. Representatives sent by each factory should be carefully selected to be physically strong, able to endure hardship, competent in travel, and have a considerable understanding of the Min and Yue dialects as a principle. It is necessary to pay attention that those suffering from infectious diseases should not go, as they may be refused landing.

Last Year's Overview of Sino-Polish Trade: Exports Increased by 7% 141

Since China and Poland signed a trade agreement, trade between the two countries has increased annually. With the rise of the port of Gdynia, built by Poland in recent years, there is a direct shipping route between Shanghai and the port, running every three weeks. At the same time, Poland has also established a commercial association in Shanghai, displaying various products and directly ordering goods on behalf of customers, which has made trade between the two sides more convenient. China's exports to Poland are mainly soybeans, sesame, tea, soybean cakes, pig bristles, tung oil, pig intestines, peanuts, and antimony. The export statistics for the previous year amounted to over 2,123,000 yuan. Poland's imports are mainly rayon, wool, wool yarn, cigarette paper, steel plates, zinc, woolen cloth, chemicals, etc. The import statistics for the previous year were approximately 1,237,000 yuan in Customs Gold Units. As for the overview of trade last year, China's exports to Poland increased by about 7% compared to the previous year. However, most of China's exports to Poland are first shipped indirectly to London, Hamburg, Amsterdam, etc., and then transshipped to Poland. The statistics for these exports are therefore included in the trade of the United Kingdom, Germany, the Netherlands, and other countries. Conversely, some goods imported from Poland are not directly shipped from the port of Gdynia to Shanghai. Therefore, the actual trade volume between the two countries is definitely more than this figure. According to customs statistics, direct imports from Poland last year amounted to 1,359,911 Customs Gold Units, an increase of 10% compared to the previous year. As far as China's total imports are concerned, Polish goods accounted for only 0.23% of imports in the previous year, but this increased to 0.25% last year.

Foreign Exchange Banking Association Notice: Deposit Interest Rates Reduced Starting Yesterday; Due to Market Stability, Monetary Conditions Gradually Loosening, and Foreign Exchange Stabilized; Uniformly 5% for Three Months, Six Months, and One Year 144

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, since the government implemented the new monetary policy and the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications have made efforts to stabilize foreign exchange, various industries have become active, the market has stabilized, and monetary conditions have gradually loosened. The Shanghai Foreign Exchange Banking Association has announced a reduction in deposit interest rates. The Chinese Bankers Association and the Chinese Money Shops Association will jointly reduce deposit and loan interest rates. The details are as follows:

Market Stability and Loosening Monetary Conditions

Since the implementation of the new monetary policy on November 4 last year, the demand for legal tender from the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications has increased sharply. The whole country is using it uniformly, and a note issuance reserve committee has been established to check and announce the reserves on a monthly basis to show credibility. The amount of money in circulation has increased, and various industries have gradually become active. Monetary conditions have gradually loosened. For example, the interbank loan rate announced in the money market yesterday was 7 fen per 1,000 yuan per day, which is lower than in previous years.

Foreign Exchange Stabilized

The Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications have made great efforts to stabilize foreign exchange, which has been quite effective. For example, the exchange rates announced by the Central Bank yesterday were: 1 shilling 2.5 pence for London, 30 US dollars for New York, 451 francs for Paris, 74 marks for Berlin, 103 yen for Japan, and 92 Hong Kong dollars, which are very stable. At the same time, various banks use the Central Bank's exchange rates as the standard for foreign exchange transactions. In addition, the Foreign Exchange Equalization Committee announced yesterday morning that the equalization tax rate was 5%.

Foreign Banks Reduce Interest Rates

The Shanghai Foreign Exchange Banking Association agreed to set fixed deposit interest rates on February 22 last year, raising them to 7% for three months, 6% for six months, and 5% for one year. On February 1 this year, in view of market stability and loosening monetary conditions, interest rates were reduced to 6% for three months, 5.5% for six months, and 5% for one year. On February 20, a further notice was issued to member banks to reduce interest rates, which will be implemented on March 1. The interest rate for current deposits (i.e., current accounts) is 2% for banks such as HSBC and Mercantile Bank.

Twenty Banks Implemented Yesterday

The foreign banks that implemented the reduction in deposit interest rates starting yesterday, i.e., member banks of the Foreign Exchange Banking Association, include: Mercantile Bank, HSBC, Chartered Bank of India, Australia and China, British Bank of the Middle East, Citibank, American Express Bank, Chase Bank, Yokohama Specie Bank, Bank of Taiwan, Bank of Chosen, Mitsui Bank, Sumitomo Bank, Mitsubishi Bank, Banque Franco-Chinoise, Banque Belge pour l'Étranger, Banque de l'Indochine, Nederlandsche Handel-Maatschappij, Banca Italo-Cinese, Deutsch-Asiatische Bank, and Banque Industrielle de Chine, a total of twenty banks.

Joint Office of Jiangbei Associations in Shanghai

The office also sent a letter to the Special Zone Office of the rickshaw industry association yesterday to request assistance. The details are as follows:

Cheng Xiechun's Talk: According to Cheng Xiechun, a member of the Jianghuai Association, since the devastation of the January 28 Shanghai Incident, followed by the wave of recession and the attack of rural bankruptcy in the interior, the employment situation has become increasingly acute. The large number of unemployed public rickshaw pullers is particularly serious. Since the two concessions in this city implemented new regulations last year, holding rickshaw puller registration and requiring the payment of one yuan and the collection of an arm badge as a proof of pulling, the time limit for registration was short, resulting in more and more rickshaw pullers who had not been registered being forced and unable to perform labor. The daily hard work and sweat of the rickshaw pullers was already insufficient to feed their families. Now, they are being subjected to such a harsh policy of high pressure and being rejected from their livelihood, which is expected. The association believes that many rickshaw pullers are fellow villagers, and since they have come to the association to request relief, they should try their best to find a way. Therefore, the Jiangbei Associations in Shanghai organized a joint office to find a way to provide relief and hope that the livelihood of unemployed rickshaw pullers will become stable. The relief measures will be discussed in detail after the registration of unemployed rickshaw pullers is completed, so that both the law and human feelings are taken care of.

Letter to the Association: The Joint Office of Jiangbei Associations in Shanghai,

Sent a letter to the Special Zone Office of the rickshaw industry association yesterday, stating that the Jiangbei Associations in Shanghai have reported that since the concession authorities held rickshaw puller registration last year and did not fully implement it, poor people from Jiangbei who came to Shanghai to pull rickshaws have been forced to become unemployed. They are wandering the streets, their livelihoods are cut off, and the situation is miserable, and they need to be relieved. Rickshaw pullers have always been free to operate rickshaws without registration. Now, they are disregarding the hardships of the workers and imposing restrictions, which not only cuts off a livelihood for poor farmers from the same village but also causes rickshaw owners to lose a lot of money due to the large number of idle rickshaws. If they do not try to remedy the situation, rickshaw owners and rickshaw pullers will perish together. The office takes the connection of village friendships and the maintenance of the public welfare of the fellow villagers as its duty and purpose. It has received calls from all sides and cannot sit idly by. It has been decided to hold registration of unemployed rickshaw pullers starting on the 22nd of this month as a basis for negotiating with the concession authorities to supplement the registration. This matter concerns the interests of both rickshaw owners and rickshaw pullers. We rely on your leadership in the special zone rickshaw industry and your concern for the hardships of rickshaw pullers. We hope that you will urge the rickshaw owners and unemployed rickshaw pullers to respond and relieve their suffering. This letter is sent to the Shanghai Rickshaw Industry Association Special Zone Office.

Nine-Province Long-Distance Telephone: The Connection Line Is Fully Completed; Tonghua Can Be Made in Jiangsu and Jiangxi-Hunan Sections 151

The long-distance telephone connection project in nine provinces, which was planned by the Ministry of Communications, has been completed. Tonghua can now be made in the Qingjiang-Zhenjiang section in Jiangsu Province and the Jiangxi-Hunan section. The Beijing-Shanghai trunk line is scheduled to be tested in the middle of next month. If the results are good, it is expected to be officially opened for business on April 1. The details are as follows:

Construction Process

In November of the 23rd year of the Republic of China, the Ministry of Communications borrowed funds from the China-British Boxer Indemnity Board of Trustees and the Postal Savings and Remittances Bureau to establish the Long-Distance Telephone Engineering Office in the nine provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hunan, Hubei, Guizhou, Fujian, and Hebei. It actively sent personnel to erect telephone lines separately. Due to the excessive length of the lines and the large scale of the project, coupled with the impact of the floods last year, the project took more than a year to complete. Now, within Jiangsu Province, such as the Qingjiang to Zhenjiang section, tonghua has been made successively since the 15th of this month, and the results are excellent. The Jiangxi and Hunan sections were also connected on the 18th.

Completed in Order

In addition, the Hunan-Hankou line was also completed yesterday. The stations along the Beijing-Shanghai line, such as Xuzhou, have long been erected. The six lines from the capital to Tianjin, Jinan to Qingdao, Xuzhou to Zhengzhou, and Hankou to Changsha were all started on the 11th of last month. The Shanghai-Hangzhou-Fujian connection line was completed later. The nine-province long-distance telephone takes Nanjing as the center. The entire project, in addition to using the original long-distance dedicated lines in the nine provinces, also built five new long-distance telephone trunk lines: Beijing-Hankou, Beijing-Tianjin, Tianjin-Qingdao, Xuzhou-Ezhou, and Ezhou-Hankou, connecting the nine provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hunan, Hubei, Guizhou, Fujian, and Hebei. It can also connect the branch lines of Hangzhou, Shanghai, Zhenjiang, Nanjing, Xuzhou, Jinan, Qingdao, Tianjin, Beiping, Zhengzhou, Kaifeng, Changsha, Hankou, Wuchang, Anqing, Nanchang, and Wuhu. In total, hundreds of places can be connected. The general engineering office is scheduled to conduct test calls with various places in the middle of next month, with Nanjing and Shanghai as the center. The various bureaus are responsible for the technical aspects of each section. If the progress is smooth, it can be opened for commercial use on April 1.

Installation of Amplifiers

This long-distance telephone line is too long. Telephone relies on the transmission of electricity, so the farther the distance, the weaker the electric waves, and the sound is not easy to be clear. The general engineering office has purchased more than one hundred amplifiers to remedy this shortcoming. Each main bureau is equipped with one amplifier, and its transmission line is released through the machine, so that its special exercise is magnified and reaches the ears of the listeners. Even if the line passes through several main bureaus, it is also amplified separately. In the future, whether communicating from Nanjing with Beiping or Tianjin, the adjustment of the sound can be the same as with city calls. Currently, the equipment has been installed in seven places, including Shanghai, Nanjing, Tianjin, Beiping, Hankou, Zhengzhou, and Xuzhou. In addition, Jinan, Qingdao, Hangzhou, etc., have also begun installation.

Public Bus Crushes a Person to Death; Investigation Underway 152

According to witness Xu Taohong's statement:

Responsibility lies with a rickshaw puller

Around 11 AM the day before yesterday, three rickshaws were traveling abreast from east to west near the Maigen Road Bridge. The rickshaw on the outside, numbered 5480, carried Zhang Songtian from Taizhou, age 41 (resident of No. 5, Zhongshan Road, Zhabei). Suddenly, the rickshaw in the middle violently bumped the outer rickshaw, causing Zhang to fall to the ground. Just then, bus No. 15049, Route 10, driven by Xu Zian, was speeding from west to east. Unable to brake in time, the front right wheel ran over Zhang, causing severe injuries. By the time the police arrived after being notified, only the rickshaw Zhang had been riding in remained; the others were gone. The Xinza Gate police station was immediately notified, and an ambulance was called to the scene. Zhang was rushed to the Binlong Hospital for treatment. Detectives were also dispatched to investigate. Unfortunately, Zhang's injuries were critical, and he died at 4 AM yesterday. The body was taken to the Philand Road morgue. Around 10 AM, Tang, a prosecutor appointed by the First Special District Court, arrived to examine the body. First, a Western officer, Zhou Weilisi, explained the situation, stating that he had questioned the rickshaw puller who had taken Zhang, who resided at No. 56, Jiesifei Road, Caojiadu. However, detectives sent to that address found no one. The deceased's address was also still unknown. Furthermore, witness Xu Taohong, a tea server at the Maigen Road People's School, testified that the accident occurred in front of the school gate, so he had witnessed it. He confirmed that the rickshaw in the middle had bumped the outer rickshaw, causing the deceased to fall and be run over by the bus. The bus was not traveling very fast, he said. After hearing the testimony, Prosecutor Tang ruled that the deceased, Zhang Songtian, male, had died from injuries sustained when he was run over by public bus No. 15049. The body was handed over to the Pushan Shanzhuang for coffin storage.

Two Opium Smokers Registered and Licensed, Disagree with the Prison Sentence 155

Why impose a criminal penalty when a limited-time smoking cessation permit has already been obtained?

Since the concession is also Chinese territory, why are the smoking prohibition regulations not applicable?

—The appeal case of Chen Arong, Xiong Sanbao, etc.—

Chen Arong, a 57-year-old Suzhou native, resided on the second floor of No. 22, Yuqing Lane, Baliqiao Road, French Concession. Xiong Sanbin, a 45-year-old local resident, resided on the third floor. The two were arrested by the French police on January 14 of this year for smoking opium and sentenced by the Second Special Court on January 25. Chen and Xiong were each sentenced to three months imprisonment and ordered to quit within one month. The two defendants disagreed with the sentence and retained lawyers Zhang Tuzhao and Wang Shizong to appeal to the Third Branch of the High Court. Their reasons are as follows: Chen Arong makes a living by selling used goods and had collected discarded lampstands, but did not use them. On that day, he asked Xiong Sanbin, who lived with him, to write a letter. He was not smoking at the time, as can be proven by the patrol officer. Since he was not caught smoking opium on the spot,

It is unjust to convict him of smoking opium.

This is the first reason for disagreement. Stepping back, even if he were smoking, the "Regulations on the Strict Prohibition of Smoking and Elimination of Smoking Households" issued by the Tobacco Control Supervisor state that those who are elderly or ill and have become addicted to smoking, and who cannot quit for the time being, may apply for registration and obtain a limited-time smoking cessation permit after being diagnosed and certified by a doctor or smoking cessation organization, allowing them to smoke temporarily, but they must gradually quit within six years, and they may not apply for an extension of the permit after the expiration date. The defendants have already followed the regulations and completed all the procedures. Thus, on the one hand, the smoking cessation organization issues a permit, allowing them to smoke because they cannot quit for the time being, and on the other hand, it strictly prohibits smoking, and all smoking is considered a crime.

Both are national organizations.

Why are they contradicting themselves in this way? Where is the credibility of the state? Furthermore, the sentence of quitting within one month is also unreasonable. If the doctor and the smoking cessation organization's certification are valid, wouldn't they be redundant? The six-year period has already been explicitly permitted, also ensuring the so-called inability to quit for the time being. In short, since this case has been dealt with in accordance with Article 8 of the Provisional Regulations on the Punishment of Smoking Offenses, the provisions of the second half of the Smoking Offenses Punishment Regulations contradict reason and law.

Furthermore, it is difficult to make people willing.

This is the second reason for disagreement. Furthermore, Article 13 of the "Regulations on the Strict Prohibition of Smoking and Elimination of Smoking Households" stipulates that those who smoke without obtaining a limited-time smoking cessation permit shall, in addition to being required to pay two to ten times the permit fee, be detained in a smoking cessation organization to verify whether they are addicted. If they are addicted, they shall be ordered to quit. Those who are elderly or ill and cannot quit for the time being may be ordered to pay the fee and obtain a supplementary permit. Those who do not obey the order to quit or do not pay the additional permit fee shall be transferred to the court for punishment according to law. Thus, the transfer to the court is for those who smoke without a permit. In addition to recovering the permit fee, they are detained in a smoking cessation organization to verify their addiction and ordered to quit.

However, those who are elderly or ill

and cannot quit for the time being may be ordered to obtain a supplementary permit. Those who do not obey the order to quit or do not pay the permit fee are punished according to law. In this case, because they are ill and cannot quit for the time being, they have a permit certified by a doctor and a smoking cessation organization. It cannot be compared to those who do not pay the permit fee. There is no need to transfer them to the court for punishment. The transfer to the court has already lost the original intention of the legislation. The court's hasty sentencing shows that it cannot understand the laws and is obviously untrue. How can people be convinced? Since this case is dealt with in accordance with Article 8 of the Provisional Regulations on the Punishment of Smoking Offenses, but the provisions of Article 19 of the same regulations are not considered,
