Suddenly, at about 7 AM yesterday morning, he hired a car from the Yunfei Car Company on Qiujiang Road, and hid a fake pistol and a pre-written letter, saying that after a few days, he had decided to borrow the money, and would return it in full after three years. He was now going to Sichuan to seek a career, so please do not pursue the matter. He drove to the door of the New Ritual Hall. A Hai entered the inner room. At that time, he saw his stepmother, Ms. Yang, lying in bed, not yet awake. A Hai immediately took out the fake pistol from his side, threatened her not to make a sound, and then rummaged through the boxes and cabinets, searching and seizing 235 yuan in legal tender and a promissory note for 300 yuan. He fled out the door. Yang's cousin, Hong Xiulin, and Ding Axin's apprentice, Xiao Chongming, saw A Hai step into the car and immediately shouted, "Catch the robber!" Patrol officer Liu Wenxin from the ninth post and police officer Ni Kehui from the thirtieth post heard the alarm and rushed over. A Hai, in desperation, used the fake pistol in the car to threaten the driver to drive quickly in an attempt to escape. He threw the hidden letter out of the car. Unexpectedly, the driver, Hu Zhongen, had already seen through the use of his fake pistol and deliberately refused to drive. When the police officers rushed into the car, they arrested Ding A Hai, seized the fake pistol, and recovered the stolen goods. They took the witnesses and the suspect back to the Dongjiadu police station. The station chief, Yi, conducted a preliminary investigation and ordered him to be detained temporarily for further investigation by the police team before being sent to the bureau for interrogation.

In the Case of the Assassination of Ji Agen, Chen Zhi is Accused of Incitement; the Judge Separately Interrogates the Witnesses; the Oral Arguments Have Concluded and the Verdict is Set for the 26th 157

Chen Zhi, a native of Jiangbei, lived at No. 271, Weixing Lane, Hengfeng Road, Zhabei. Having lived in Shanghai for more than thirty years, he operated a number of businesses in the Zhabei area, including real estate, rickshaw companies, and bathhouses, and recruited a large number of followers, numbering several thousand. Therefore, he had the nickname "Jiangbei Big Boss of Zhabei." Recently, Yao Gonglin, the murderer of Ji Agen, a former detective of the Kunshan County Detective Team, identified Chen as the instigator of the case. The Xinza Gate Public Security Bureau investigated, but for a long time, they did not make any progress. Last winter, Chen suddenly surrendered himself to the court. After investigation by the prosecutor, Chen was publicly prosecuted according to Article 271 of the Criminal Law for the crime of inciting murder. Judge Li of the Criminal Court has already questioned him. Because there were matters to investigate with the detective team and public security bureau personnel who handled the Yao Gonglin case, he ordered the defendant to pay a store guarantee of 30,000 yuan, and postponed the hearing. Recently, the hearing was resumed, and all the witnesses were summoned to testify. The oral arguments were concluded in court, and the verdict was set for the 26th of this month. The details of the trial are recorded below:

Shi Zuhan At 10:20 AM yesterday morning, Judge Li ascended to the seat in the Fifth Criminal Court and ordered the court clerks to bring the plaintiff and defendant to the court. After questioning them one by one about their age, origin, address, and occupation, he instructed the defendant Chen Zhiyi, "In order to clarify the truth in this case, this court has retrieved the files of the murderer Yao Gonglin and the plaintiff Ji Wang's statements in the Public Security Bureau, and the personnel handling this case have also been summoned. Today, the testimony of the witnesses must be interrogated separately." After the order was completed, Chen Zhi was ordered to retreat to the waiting room. First, Shi Zuhan, the leader of the detective squad handling the case, was brought to the court. He was instructed, "This court summoned you to testify today because you handled the Yao Gonglin murder case. You must tell the truth. If you say anything false, you will be prosecuted for perjury." Shi then testified, "I am 27 years old, a native of Hang County, and the leader of the squad in the Xinza Gate Public Security Bureau of the Municipal Public Security Bureau Detective Team. At 2:22 PM on July 22nd last year, I received a call from the Central Police Station of the Public Concession, saying that the murderer Yao Gonglin, who killed Ji Agen, was seen by Ji's wife, Wang, and had been brought into the police station. After receiving this call, I sent someone to the police station to transfer the plaintiff and defendant to the team. Because it was late that day, our detective team did not have a detention center, so we sent him to the Xinza Gate Sub-bureau for detention. The next day, we transferred him to the team for interrogation." Judge Li asked, "Did you use torture when you interrogated Yao Gonglin?" Shi answered, "We don't use torture in any case. However, the plaintiff Ji Wang said two sentences to Yao Gonglin during the interrogation, which I suspected very much." The judge asked, "What did she say?" He answered, "She said to Yao Gonglin, 'Now that things have come to this, you should tell me quickly, whether it was I who had a feud with my husband, or someone else who hired you to kill my husband.'" The judge asked, "Then how did Yao Gonglin answer?" He answered, "Yao Gonglin said to her, 'It was not my intention to kill your husband. It was Chen Zhi who instructed me.' When I heard this, I ordered the detective Mao Gongzhao to take Ji Wang out, fearing that Ji Wang would instigate Yao Gonglin to falsely accuse Chen Zhi. After Ji Wang left, I interrogated him in detail." The judge asked, "Did you use torture at this time?" He answered, "I didn't use torture, but I scared him. I said, 'Tell me the truth honestly. Don't wrong anyone. If you tell a lie, I won't be polite.' I asked him three or four times like that, and he still said that Chen Zhi had instigated him. I said, 'Since you say it was Chen Zhi, can you point him out?' He said he could. So I led the detectives to the Haiqing Bathhouse to arrest Chen, but he was not there. The bathhouse staff said that the boss was in his residence in Weixing Lane, Hengfeng Road, and had not come out. So we went to arrest him at his address, but we still didn't find him. According to his family, he had gone to Jiangbei. Therefore, Chen Zhi and the fugitives Jia Abao and Zhou Longkouzi were not arrested. Yao Gonglin was sent to the bureau and transferred to your court for interrogation. I don't know anything else."

Huang Chongren Subsequently, Huang Chongren, a member of the Xinza Gate Public Security Bureau, was summoned. He testified, "I am 38 years old, a native of Hunan." The judge asked, "Was it you who questioned Ji Wang about Yao Gonglin killing her husband?" Huang answered, "It was me who questioned her, but it was too long ago, it was last July. Moreover, there are many cases in our bureau, at least three or four every day. I have completely forgotten the details of this case. Your court sent me a subpoena earlier, asking me to come to court to testify. Our documents section is looking at the case file, but the file has been retrieved by your court. I don't know which aspect of the testimony the court wants me to prove now." The judge said, "Just tell the truth and don't favor any party. If you don't remember clearly, the testimony you took from them at that time is in the file here. You can take a look first." Huang then took the file and looked through it and said to the judge, "Everything I remember is in the file. I can't remember anything outside of the file." The judge asked, "When you questioned Yao Gonglin, did you use torture or threats?" Huang answered, "When we question cases, we don't talk about threats or torture at all. When Yao Gonglin arrived at the bureau, as soon as I asked him, he said what he had said in the detective team." The judge asked, "Is the testimony recorded on the approval form the same as the testimony he gave?" Huang answered, "Of course it is."

Lin Zhaowu Judge Li then turned to Lin Zhaowu, the chief of the interrogation section of the Third Section of the Public Security Bureau, and asked, "Was it you who questioned Yao Gonglin when the Yao Gonglin murder case was sent to the general bureau?" Lin answered, "Yes." The judge asked, "Since it was you who questioned him, do you still remember it clearly?" He answered, "I can't remember all the details of the case. I only remember that when I asked Yao Gonglin, he did not admit that he had killed Ji Agen. He only said that he saw Jia Ashi point a pistol at Ji Wang and not allow her to make a sound." The judge asked, "Did Yao Gonglin say that Chen Zhi was the instigator, that Ji Wang told him to say that, or did he say it himself, or did you use torture or threats to get him to say it?" He answered, "I didn't hear Ji Wang tell him to say it. We never use threats or torture when we interrogate cases. We record what the parties say."

Ji Wangshi The judge then turned to the plaintiff Ji Wangshi and asked, "Why did you say to Yao Gonglin in the detective team, 'Did I hire someone to kill my husband, or did someone else instigate it?'" Ji Wangshi answered, "I really didn't say anything like that. I only sent the bureau the list of murderers who had been filed when my husband was killed and requested that they be handled according to law to redress my husband's grievances. I had never heard of Chen Zhi as the instigator before Yao Gonglin was arrested. He is a famous Jiangbei Big Boss of Zhabei. If I had known, I would have sued him long ago. That's what Yao Gonglin said to me when I grabbed him. He said, 'You only抓 者 me, why don't you catch Chen Zhi?' That was when I first knew that in the detective team, Yao Gonglin had said that Chen Zhi was the instigator. The people in the detective team certainly didn't say good things about me and took me out because detectives like Mao Gongzhao are all Chen Zhi's disciples. Hearing that Yao Gonglin was biting their old man, they were certainly dissatisfied. Now your court prosecutor's office is prosecuting Chen Zhi for inciting murder according to Article 271 of the Criminal Law, which is a major case. How can he be released on bail?" The judge said, "This is a legal study. We think he can be released on bail. You don't understand the law and don't need to pursue it. Regarding the incidental private prosecution, you withdrew it yourself last time and then applied to restore the original state, but this is a legal procedure and has not been completed. What is your decision now? Your private prosecution lawyer is also not here." Ji Wangshi answered, "My lawyer, Fei Guoxi, often goes to Chen Zhi's Haiqing Pool to bathe and is afraid to come. I can't think of any way to proceed with the private prosecution. Please rule according to law."

Chen Zhi At this point, the judge ordered the defendant Chen Zhi to be brought to the court and instructed him, "The witnesses summoned to the court today are the captain of the detective squad, the director of the Xinza Gate Branch, and the director of the investigation section of the Third Section of the Public Security Bureau. They are all the personnel in charge of Ji Wang's lawsuit against Yao Gonglin. Their testimony is that Yao Gonglin said you were the instigator and that it was not obtained through torture or threats. It was all Yao Gonglin who said it himself. What do you have to say in response?" Chen Zhi answered, "I am an honest businessman and have always held a charitable and moral heart. Even a dog's life is a life, let alone a human being. I am already in my fifties and have children. How could I do such a conscience-less thing? Yao Gonglin was originally a disciple of Yang Wenbin, the leader of the detective team in Kunshan County. I sued Yang Wenbin. He was sentenced to a crime. He would be taking revenge for his old man by biting me. The court must not adopt his testimony." The judge asked, "What do you have to say about the private prosecution?" Chen answered, "Ji Wangshi herself wanted to withdraw it before the trial. She doesn't want the money, so I don't need to answer." At this point, Judge Li ordered the court clerk to invite the prosecutor to the court to argue the case and instructed the defendant's defense lawyer to begin the argument. This took an hour. Judge Li then announced, "The arguments in this case are concluded, and the verdict will be announced on the 26th of this month. The defendant will remain on the original bail." Then he adjourned the court.

Chinese Republic Lawyers Association Held Sixth General Meeting Yesterday to Discuss Various Motions, Decide on Secretary-General, and Hold Closing Ceremony This Afternoon 158

Morning Meeting: The seventh session of the Chinese Republic Lawyers Association Representative Assembly was held yesterday (the 21st) at 9:30 AM at the China Arts and Crafts Society, holding its sixth plenary session. Representatives from various local lawyers' associations attended: Zhang Shijie, Dai Tianqiu, Li Hong, Cao Huiru, Cai Shenghuan, Shen Yingshi, Li Han, Yu Naiduo, Mou Shaozhou, Liu Zeyi, Chen Zhi, Hu Zongxin, Pu Fengying, Hua Chun'an, Mi Wenxiao, Chang Yunpeng, Zhou Zhenfan, Cha Renwei, Chen Liubo, Wu Weihuan, Lei Wanpeng, Li Keyu, Qiu Zhaowen, Zheng Ruizhang, Zhang Tao, Chen Dexin, Xu Honghuan, Sha Xunyi, Zhang Bingyang, Jiang Yong, Cai Li, Zhu YaKui, Wu Zengshan, Bo Zhu, Zhuang Xiang, Xu Jun, Liu Zuwang, Wang Weizhen, Liu Zhe, Yu Zhongluo, Tan Yigong, Kuai Jinde, Chen Mingjian, Xu Kezhi, Gong Shengzhi, Yan Yinwu, Zhu Fujiu, Sun Zuji, Sun Chunhai, Ruan Shou, Zhang Mo, Zhang Mingdong, Chen Liren, Huang Rongchang, Chen Tingrui, Jiang Yiping, Hu Jue, Yuan Yang'an, Wu Luping, Shen Junru, etc. The director of the General Assembly Secretariat was also present. Zheng Yue was sent by the Ministry of Judicial Administration to attend the meeting. He rang the bell to start the meeting. Zhang Tao, the representative of the Hangzhou County Association, was elected as the chairman. Ji Xian was the secretary. The meeting proceeded as usual. The details are recorded below. The chairman reported that the association has a total of sixty-eight member associations, and representatives from forty-three associations were present today, which is sufficient for a quorum, and declared the meeting open. Zhang Shijie, director of the procedural group, reported on the resolutions of the fifth general meeting and read them out one by one. The chairman reported that Shen Honglie, the mayor of Qingdao, had sent a telegram to congratulate the assembly. (Resolved) A reply telegram will be sent to thank him. The presidium Qiu Zhaowen took the stage to report on the opinions of the seven representatives of the presidium Liu Liumin, Li Hongyue, Chen Mingjian, Mou Shaozhou, Shen Junru, and Qiu Zhaowen who reviewed five proposals last night, and then the discussion of the proposals began. (A) The Capital Lawyers Association proposed that there should be a definite method for inspecting opium smokers. The review opinion was to pass the original proposal. It was resolved to pass the review opinion. (B) The three lawyers' associations of Shaoxing, Hangzhou, and Yin County in Zhejiang province proposed to request the Ministry of Judicial Administration to issue a notice to all levels of courts to accept the pleadings prepared by lawyers and exempt them from the pleading fee in order to comply with laws and regulations. The review opinion was that this was a unique event in Shaoxing, and the Executive Committee should send a letter to the Zhejiang Higher Court, ordering the Shaoxing Local Court to abolish the pleading fee. It was resolved to pass the proposal. (C) The Songjiang Lawyers Association proposed that the court should respect the personality and treatment of lawyers. The review opinion was that the principle of this case has been adopted in the draft Lawyers Law drafted by the association and should be retained. It was resolved to handle it together with the draft of the Lawyers Law itself. (D) The County Lawyers Association proposed to amend the association's charter to conform to the actual name. The review opinion was that it concerned the amendment of the association's charter, and there was no endorsement of more than one-third of the members, so the procedure was not in compliance and should be retained. It was resolved to pass the review opinion. (E) The Shanghai Lawyers Association suggested that the highest judicial authority should coordinate with the foreign authorities to seek to abolish or improve the existing agreements made by the Shanghai Public Concession and the French Concession, which are about to expire, so as to unify the national trial system and complete national sovereignty. The review opinion was to refer it to the Executive Committee for handling. It was resolved to handle it according to the review opinion. Temporary motions: (A) The Yin County Lawyers Association suggested that the Ministry of Judicial Administration should be requested to order all local lawyers' associations to join the association. It was resolved to pass the proposal. (B) The Shanghai Lawyers Association proposed that the General Assembly should decide on Article 5 of the Association's Charter, the selection of representatives, and Article 16, the supplementary measures for concurrent positions. It was resolved that it was not established. (C) The Songjiang Lawyers Association suggested that the Legislative Yuan should be requested to amend Article 368 of the Criminal Procedure Law. It was resolved to pass it in principle and refer it to the Executive Committee for handling. (D) The Shanghai Lawyers Association proposed that the Ministry of Judicial Administration should submit to the Judicial Yuan to request the Legislative Yuan to amend Article 681 of the Civil Law on Obligations. Because this case is of great importance, it was resolved to refer it to the Executive and Supervisory Committee for consideration and handling. (E) The Wu County Lawyers Association proposed that the association should notify all lawyers' associations to stop lawyers from setting up branch offices and correspondence addresses, and to rectify the clerks in order to maintain discipline. It was mistakenly recorded yesterday as submitting it to the Ministry of Justice. In fact, it was resolved that the association should forward it to the various master lawyers' associations. The meeting adjourned at twelve o'clock.

City Council Suggests Unifying Licensing Procedures in This City. The City Government Has Replied After Review by Various Bureaus. 160

The various registrations and licenses handled by the bureaus in this city are extremely cumbersome. There are fourteen types issued directly by the Social Affairs Bureau or transferred by the Social Affairs Bureau to the Ministry of Industry. Nineteen types are issued by the Public Security Bureau. Eleven types are issued by the Finance Bureau. Seven types are issued by the Public Works Bureau. Eighteen types are issued by the Health Bureau. Ten types, totaling six types, are issued by the Public Utilities Bureau, totaling eighty-five types. Citizens are not clear about the procedures and nature, and often have to run around several places to apply for a license. The City Council of this city, in view of this, has specifically requested the City Government to unify the licensing procedures to benefit citizens. The City Government immediately handed it over to the relevant bureaus for review, and it has been reported jointly by the bureaus. All licenses issued are of a temporary nature and only related to one bureau, and are issued by that bureau. If they are of a permanent nature and related to more than two bureaus, the principle of obtaining one license should be followed. Licenses issued are subject to the regulations and must be reviewed by the relevant bureaus, and the old procedures should still be followed. The name of a certain license that has been agreed upon should be reported by a certain bureau. The licenses issued by various bureaus are replaced annually, or only issued once and do not need to be replaced annually, or inspected annually after issuance, which is not consistent. For the sake of uniformity and simplicity, except for the donation licenses issued by the Finance Bureau, which are receipts, and the medical, pharmaceutical, food, and beverage licenses issued by the Health Bureau, which will continue to be handled as before and cannot be changed, the remaining licenses will be changed to annual inspections, which has been replied to by the City Government to the City Council.

The Paper Industry in Shanghai (4) 165

— Edited by China Huixin

(Overview of Industry and Commerce in Shanghai XIV)

5. Paper Market Conditions in the Past Year and Recently: In terms of the past year, the paper industry in various countries around the world has shown signs of improvement and prosperity. For example, the paper mills in major paper-producing countries such as the United States, Canada, Sweden, and Norway are all operating their paper machines at full speed. The only difference is that paper prices have not risen in the same proportion. As for China (especially Shanghai), its market conditions have generally declined, with the exception of the first four months. From January to March, the foreign paper market in this city was very active, and the import volume of foreign paper from the United States and Canada was very large. However, from the end of March, partly due to rumors of tariff revisions, market demand suddenly declined, and there was almost no sales in South China and North China. What cannot be ignored in this is that Japanese paper is selling well in various parts of North China. By October, the situation changed drastically, because rumors of new currency policies were rampant, and paper prices were soaring. At that time, six small import merchants suffered heavy losses in foreign exchange due to the fact that they had not paid for overseas orders, resulting in bankruptcy, because the foreign exchange against the pound sterling had fallen from 18 pence to 14 pence at that time. Before and after the promulgation of the new legal tender, the ups and downs of paper prices in this city were very significant. Now, several types of paper are selected and listed for comparison as follows:

October 8 October 20 November Estimated Value 4 Estimated Value Price Price Price White Writing Paper Per Ream 2 Yuan 3.50 Yuan 2.75 Yuan 2.50 Yuan Newsprint Roll Per Ream 2 Yuan 3.20 Yuan 3.60 Yuan 4.00 Yuan Daolin Paper Per Kilogram 0.22 Yuan 0.23 Yuan 0.24 Yuan 0.015 Yuan Small Waxed Paper Per Ream 10 Yuan 11 Yuan 12.50 Yuan Kraft Paper Per Ream 6 Yuan 7 Yuan 8 Yuan 0.32 Yuan

Note: Estimated value is the price assessed by the Paper Industry Association, which is the standard for general market prices.

Recently, various paper prices have shown a slight downward trend due to sluggish sales, especially Lian Shi paper and Mao Bian paper, because the domestically produced Lian Shi paper and Mao Bian paper are also very fine and can compete with Japanese goods. At present, various manufacturers also intend to compete with Japanese goods, so their market prices have fallen more. The latest survey results are listed below:

Da Zhonghua Su Shi, from 3.10 yuan to 3.60 yuan per ream, the selling price of Mao Bian is the same.

Baoshan Su Shi and Mao Bian, the top grade is 3.56 yuan per ream, the middle grade is 3.23 yuan, and the bottom grade is 2.90 yuan.

Shanghai Lian Shi, from 3 yuan to 3.50 yuan per ream, Mao Bian, from 3.10 yuan to 3.30 yuan.

Yuan Tai Sen Ji Lian Shi Mao Bian sells for 3.10 yuan to 3.20 yuan per ream.

The selling price of Jiangnan Lian Shi Mao Bian is still the price set in August last year. The smallest Lian Shi is 3.75 yuan per ream, and the largest is 4.67 yuan, which is about one yuan higher than the products of other factories.

Tian Zhang Chang Ji Daolin paper sells for 0.11 yuan per pound (less commission), the price of drawing paper is the same as the price of writing paper.

Long Zhang Daolin paper, 0.18 yuan per pound (less 96 or 97 discount, paper merchants can get a discount when buying goods from the company). The selling price of Lian Shi produced by the company also varies from 6.50 yuan to 13.10 yuan per piece due to different packaging (some are 10 knives per piece, some are 15 knives per piece, and the most are 44 knives per piece).

Mei Jin Small Waxed Paper sells for 10 yuan per ream, Yellow Paperboard sells for more than 80 yuan per ton (wholesale price 74 yuan), and Gray Newsprint sells for 2.20 yuan per ream (wholesale price 2 yuan).

Recently, the sales of Lian Shi Mao Bian have been very good. It is said that the sales of ordinary goods with low prices are the most (such as those selling for 3 yuan to 3.12 yuan). Various paper mills are rushing to manufacture due to insufficient supply, which is very busy. Among them, Baoshan, Da Zhonghua, and Shanghai factories are the most developed. (End)

Liang Weichu Was Slashed Fourteen Times by Enemies. The Bloody Case in Front of the Shanghai Grand Theater. Dying, Reportedly Due to a Love Triangle. 166

Liang Weichu, a Cantonese man, 26 years old, lived at No. 15, Shutahe Lane, Beishansi Road. Yesterday afternoon, Liang and one or two friends went to the Shanghai Grand Theater at the intersection of Beisichuan Road and Qiujiang Road to watch a movie. Waiting until 4:40 PM, after watching the movie, he went out. Unexpectedly, just as he was about to exit, stepping down the stone steps, and turning the corner, three or four teenagers protruded from the corner of the wall, holding sharp axes, and slashed at Liang. Liang was caught off guard and was hit four times in the right hand, seven times in the left leg, and three times in the head. Blood poured out immediately, and he fell to the ground dying. The murderer, seeing that the goal had been achieved, fled into the alley. His friend rushed him to the hospital for treatment, but never reported it to the police. Therefore, the hospital immediately notified the police station and sent detectives to the hospital to investigate. Because the friend was very suspicious, he was summoned to the police station for interrogation. It is reported that it was caused by a love triangle. The police station is still investigating strictly.

Executive Yuan Orders Prohibition of Activities by the Beiping-Tianjin Student Union; Confirmed That a Small Number of Malicious Elements Are in Control 175

(Central News Agency, Nanjing, 21st) According to recent confidential reports received by the central government, a small number of malicious elements are indeed in control of the Beiping-Tianjin Student Union. They are repeatedly plotting to instigate student unrest in various schools. In order to rectify academic conduct and allow the majority of pure youths to study in peace and strengthen their abilities, it has been decided to prohibit the activities of the Student Union. On the 21st, the Executive Yuan specifically ordered the Ministry of Education to investigate the organization of the Beiping-Tianjin Student Union, which has no legal basis, and to report on the fact that a small number of malicious elements are secretly manipulating and inciting unrest. In order to protect the majority of pure youths and prevent them from being coerced, the central government should immediately prohibit the activities of the Student Union in order to promote academic integrity. The Ministry of Education should quickly comply and handle the matter carefully. After receiving the order, the Ministry of Education has already notified the authorities in Beiping and Tianjin to comply.

Yunnan Province Implements Education for the Miao People 181

After the central government decided to allocate 90,000 yuan to Yunnan Province from the frontier education assistance fund for the 24th year, the provincial Department of Education used 24,000 yuan to establish Miao elementary schools and 25,000 yuan to train Miao teachers. The remaining funds were used for compulsory education expenses. The province plans to establish schools and encourage enrollment in areas where the Miao people reside, where education is underdeveloped, and where the language has not yet been unified (such as the Dianzhong Road District, Mengzi Road District, the Panjiang River Basin in eastern Yunnan, the Tengyong southwest region, and along the border and in over forty other places). The aim is to gradually improve the level of education and culture in the area so that it becomes the same as in the inland areas. Provincial simplified normal schools will also be established in Deqin (Atuntze), Tengyue, Mianning, or Zhenkang, Cheli, Kaihua, etc., to offer regular classes or first one-to-two-year teacher training classes, and attached elementary schools will be established. Provincial elementary schools will be established in Zhongdian, Weixi, Fugong, Gongshan, Bijiang, Lanping, Luyong, Lianghe, Yingjiang, Luxi, Lianshan, Longchuan, Ruili, Zhenkang, Shuangjiang, Lancang, Cangyuan, Ningjiang, Dashun, Fohai, Nanjiao, Zhenyue, Jiangcheng, Jinping, Hekou, Qiubei, Fuzhou, Yanshan, and Dachengba, and one-to-two-year teacher training classes will also be offered (except for Kaihua, the above-listed schools will all be established and start classes in February of this year). The main focus of this Miao education is to learn Mandarin Chinese, but for the convenience of teaching, the local language may be used at the beginning of learning in order to gradually correct it.

National Children's Painting Exhibition Scheduled; Organizational Rules for the Judging Committee Established; Article 5 of the Detailed Rules for Submissions Revised; Yesterday's Telegram to the National Children's Year Implementation Committee 183

The National Children's Painting Exhibition is scheduled to be held at the city center sports field starting on June 6th. The organizational rules for the Judging Committee have been established, and Article 5 of the Detailed Rules for Submissions has also been revised. The details are as follows:

Judging Committee Rules

Article 1: This committee is organized in accordance with Article 9 of the Outline of Measures for the National Children's Painting Exhibition and Article 10 of the Detailed Rules for Collection of Works.

Article 2: This committee will have a number of members. In addition to the head of the judging section of the organizing committee being an ex officio member, the others will be selected by the organizing committee and then appointed by the National Children's Year Implementation Committee.

Article 3: The tasks of this committee are as follows:

* Reviewing matters related to submissions (standards to be set separately).

* Judging matters related to submissions (standards to be set separately).

* Collaborating with the display section to design display matters.

* Discussing reward and punishment matters.

* Studying the content of submissions.

* Preparing a judging report.

Article 4: The convening of meetings and the review and judging of matters by this committee shall be handled by the judging section of the organizing committee.

Article 5: The judging committee members serve as volunteers. However, out-of-town members may be given travel expenses when attending meetings.

Article 6: These rules will be implemented after being approved by the organizing committee. If there are any imperfections, the organizing committee may modify them at any time.

Revised Detailed Rules for Submissions: The association began collecting submissions from public and private elementary schools and kindergartens across the country on the 10th of this month. Article 5 of the original Detailed Rules for Submissions, which stipulated the size of the paintings to be 26 cm wide and 20 cm high, has been changed to no specifications in order to facilitate children's free expression, as decided by the third preparatory meeting. The association specifically telegraphed the National Children's Year Implementation Committee yesterday to request the revision. The original telegram is as follows: To the Ministry of Education of Nanjing, forwarded to the National Children's Year Implementation Committee, regarding Article 5 of the Painting Exhibition Detailed Rules for Submissions, the size has been changed to no specifications. National Children's Painting Exhibition Preparatory Committee.

County Education Bureau Establishes Measures for the Second Phase of Literacy Education 189

The Shanghai County Education Bureau convened a meeting of directors of social education agencies yesterday to discuss measures for the second phase of literacy schools, as the first phase had already concluded. The resolutions are as follows:

* The passing standard for student performance in this phase of literacy schools: The committee decided that a score of 60 points and attendance of at least two-thirds of the time are required to pass.

* In addition to issuing literacy certificates to passing students in this phase of literacy schools, a list of students who should have enrolled in this phase but did not and those who failed this phase should be selected and sent to the bureau: The committee decided to pass this proposal. Each school should prepare two copies of the list, one to be submitted to the Education Bureau and one to be submitted to the Township Popular Literacy Education Committee.

* Drafting points of attention for handling the second phase of literacy schools: The committee decided to establish the following:

* (A) Enrollment:

* Those who should have enrolled in the first phase but did not.

* Those who enrolled in the first phase but did not obtain a literacy certificate.

* Illiterate adults over the age of sixteen.

* Illiterate village heads and heads of jia.

* Literate adults and school-age children will not be recruited. Each class should aim to recruit 50 people.

* (B) Administration:

* The principal should be concurrently held by the bao chief, with one school per bao.

* The school site should be designated by the bao chief at a suitable location and reported to the district Popular Literacy Education Committee for forwarding to the Education Bureau.

* Equipment: Each school should have at least one portrait of President Sun Yat-sen, one small blackboard, and one attendance book. Desks and chairs should be borrowed by the bao chief.

* (C) Education:

* The principal should serve concurrently, with the Township Popular Literacy Education Committee hiring the principal. Teaching is on a voluntary basis.

* A student register must also be prepared, with attention to filling in items such as baojia, household rice, etc.

* The required expenses should be raised and used by the township office.

* (D) Teaching:

* Literacy instruction should be at least one hour per day, and time may be added for talks, lectures on civic common sense, baojia knowledge, etc.

* The daily class schedule may be determined by each school and reported to the district Popular Education Committee for record.

* Teachers should conduct home visits and pay attention to urging absent students.

* The teaching attitude should be sincere, patient, humble, and harmonious.

Children's Educational Novel

Little Men (1) (8) (3) 191

— Original by Louisa M. Alcott, Translated by Zheng Xiaocang

After a few weeks at home, Nat came back to school, looking as if he had recovered from his grief. This was due in no small part to the adaptable nature of childhood. He had certainly recovered to some extent; he did not forget, because his nature was such that whatever happened to him was deeply absorbed, carefully filtered, and then permeated to the innermost spring, to irrigate his sensitive mind and nurture his various small virtues. He played, studied, worked, and sometimes sang, all as usual, and it was not easy for others to guess at what changes had taken place. But there was one person, Aunt Jo, who had seen it, because she watched the boy with all her heart, wanting to take John’s place herself. It was truly a labor of love. He rarely spoke of his loss, but Aunt Jo often heard soft sobs coming from the small bed at night. When she went to comfort him, he would only cry out, "I want my father, oh, I want my father!" — the connection between them was so close and beautiful that when it was broken, the boy's heart was also broken. But "Time" gradually filled his wounds, and he gradually felt that he had not lost his father, but only temporarily hidden him, and that he would see him again one day, just as strong and kind, although his little son would have to see the purple asters bloom and fall many, many times on his father's grave before they could meet again.

The external changes kept pace with the internal changes, because in those few weeks, Nat seemed to have grown up and had begun to abandon his childish games. Not because he was ashamed of them, as some children feel, but because his interests had outgrown them and he needed something more suited to adults. He began to love arithmetic, which he had always hated, and studied it tirelessly. His uncle was pleasantly surprised, but did not understand the source of his new interest until Plum said:

"When I grow up, I want to be an accountant like Dad, so I have to understand arithmetic and things like that, or I won't be able to have his kind of clear and neat books."

Commercial News

Finance: Gold Market Dull and Lifeless 192

Turnover Less Than Three Thousand, Swap Premium Slightly Lower

The gold market showed no sign of improvement yesterday. Transactions were sporadic, with fluctuations of only 1.10 yuan. The future market hovered around 4 jiao. The foreign exchange market eased and the trend weakened slightly. The outlook is bleak. In the early morning, after overseas silver markets saw London fall and the US remain flat, there was talk that there were sellers at the quoted price but no transactions. Monte di Righi silver forward prices fell by 0.05 to 0.10 tael. London spot gold rose by 0.5 pence. Exchange rates were mixed. The Central Bank's quoted price rose to 1147.10 yuan, but due to a lack of interest, no transactions were opened outside the market in anticipation of trading. Transactions began at 9:05 AM, opening at the same price as the previous day. After the opening, prices remained stable. Later, due to large buyers withdrawing and providing supply, the HSBC quoted price, although unchanged, was slightly lower. Banks were selling. The silver balance tax revealed a decrease of 0.025, and the trend was difficult to support, but still hovered. The foreign exchange market remained loose, and selling pressure eventually prevailed, gradually declining. Mobil Oil concluded its purchases of US dollars, and after falling, gradually leveled off. After entering, the demand for supply balanced, and fluctuations were limited. The noon market was also very stable. In the afternoon, the market situation seemed stable, with fluctuations of only 0.04 jiao. Although large traders were divesting, banks were settling prior orders, and buying interest was also strong. Finally, prices stabilized and the swap premium rose slightly. The three-to-four-month swap rose to 4.60 yuan. A record of today's market situation follows.

The opening price in the morning was 1148.40 yuan, the same as the previous closing price. Kang Richang, Tianfa, and others offered, rising from 8.30 yuan to 8.60 yuan. Tong Feng, Hengda, Changxiang, Fusheng, Yongding, and Kangyuan Fengyong divested. Although the HSBC quoted price was flat, Citibank sold February US dollars at 1.875, but still retreated to 8 yuan. Dadecheng, Yuanmaoyong, and others offered, rising to 8.20 yuan. Tong Feng, Hengtai, Changqian, and Changxiang sold again at 8 yuan. The silver balance tax revealed a decrease of 0.025. At this time, due to a slight increase of 0.01 yuan, the market was still hovering. Mitsui sold March US dollars at 0.0625. Yuanmaoyong, Jingfu, Fengchang, Ju Dahui, Xiangfuxingyong sold successively, falling to 7.50 yuan. Mobil Oil tentatively priced March US dollars at 0.0625. Yingfeng, Hengchunyuanyong bought slightly, rising to 7.80 yuan. Fuxingyong and Yuanmaoyong Richang continued to sell, further falling to 7.50 yuan. Qingfa and Yongda Changxiang bought slightly. The noon closing price was 1147.60 yuan.

The afternoon market opened at 1147.60 yuan. Dadecheng Dingkang and others offered, rising to 7.70 yuan. Yongsang sold to 7.60 yuan. Dadecheng, Huixiang, and others offered, rising to 7.90 yuan. Yuanmaoyong sold again for 7.80 yuan. Shanghai priced March pounds at 4.375 and 0.5 pence for pairing. Houyudingkang Richang advanced to 8 yuan. Jingfu Chunyuanyong sold coupons, retreating to 7.90 yuan. Qiaofeng Yong scattered customers sold coupons, rising to 8 yuan. Jingfu continued to sell. The closing price was 1147.90 yuan.

The settlement price was 1147.30 yuan according to the Central Bank's quoted standard gold price. The Silk Industry in the Past Year (Continued Part 2) 213

— Wang Tianyu

Shanghai exported 48,088 bales of raw silk in the eleven months from January to November, more than double the amount from last year. Guangdong, on the other hand, saw a decrease in exports, with only 18,192 bales. Domestic sales were approximately 10,000 bales, a 50% decrease from last year.

In summary, although the silk industry in 1935 went from a depression in the first half of the year to a boom in the second half, domestic workers were mostly rejoicing. However, under such favorable conditions, many silk factories were forced to close due to a lack of raw materials. This was because: first, the stagnation of silk sales and the sharp fall in silk prices in recent years led to a widespread aversion to sericulture among farmers, resulting in the felling of mulberry trees and planting of crops, reducing mulberry orchards in Jiangsu and Zhejiang by about one-third. Second, the government restricted the production of various silk worm species in 1935, having learned a lesson from the oversupply of autumn seeds in the autumn of 1934, without considering that the previous lesson was under special drought conditions. This resulted in an unprecedented shortage of silk worm eggs, with farmers raising silk worms but lacking the silk worm eggs to feed them. Therefore, although the silk industry in 1935 had a more favorable opportunity, the problem of raw material production became the only regret.

(3)

We know that the rise in silk prices in 1935 was mainly due to the stimulus of increased consumption, but other negative reasons also contributed to the fluctuation of silk prices. We can divide this into several aspects:

The first is the turning point in the world economy. The world economy's transition from "panic" to "depression" was not a normal turning point, but rather a boom in military demand triggered by the "gunpowder smell" of international instability and heightened contradictions. This boom was not enough to drive the entire economy, but it stimulated a small increase in silk consumption. The increase in US consumption cannot be said to be due to this. The proportion of unemployed workers joining the labor union alliance rebounded and decreased, and the number of workers employed in all factories also increased slightly. Although it was not as good as in 1930, the slight decrease in unemployment was enough to increase consumption. (To be continued)

Page 18

Women's Special Issue

The Modern Standard Woman 214

— Jing

Women's liberation is generally described as "going to serve society." Indeed, women serving society is liberation, but it is a mistake to limit the word "liberation" solely to serving society. In my opinion, it is right for women to adequately serve society under the banner of liberation. However, if liberation is solely equated with serving society as a woman's only duty, and everything else is disregarded, then that is wrong.

An example occurred recently in the family of a friend of mine. My friend's wife is a new woman who received a full education and has also led small-scale women's movements. After marrying my friend, she took a job at an organization immediately after their honeymoon. At home, they have two maids responsible for washing and cooking. As for herself, in her spare time, she only drags her husband out to play. If her husband is not happy to go, she goes out alone.

My friend, though not stubborn, enjoys a leisurely family life. Initially, he thought that after marrying her, they could enjoy some marital happiness after finishing their work, but after marriage, his wife still loved to play so much that he inevitably found it quite distressing. So, he slightly advised her. Little did he know that he would greatly offend his wife, who said, "If you want a wife who is like a slave, you should look for her in the countryside."

After being married for a year, she suddenly became pregnant last autumn. My friend had always felt too lonely at home, so he was very happy to learn that she was pregnant. Unexpectedly, after a few days, she secretly had an abortion. My friend strongly disapproved, and the feelings between the two gradually deteriorated. His wife's only reason was, "Asking me to be a virtuous mother and good wife of the 19th century is out of the question."

From this example, it seems that "virtuous mother and good wife" is not worth half a penny in the eyes of modern women. However, look, there is a widespread slogan in Germany now, "Women return to the family." Returning to the family, what do they do? Naturally, it is "managing household affairs" and "raising children." "Managing household affairs" and "raising children," although not directly serving society, are indirectly contributing to the survival of the nation. And in practice, it may be more effective than directly serving society.

Soviet Russia, as we have always known, is a socialist country that does not pay attention to the family system. Soviet women work the same as men. However, according to recent surveys, the government has restricted behaviors that damage family organization, such as divorce, abortion, and neglecting child support. At the same time, families preparing their own meals have also increased considerably. The business of more than 200 workers' dormitories and more than 300 public canteens in Moscow and its suburbs has declined by about 40% compared to three years ago. Nurseries, however, are developing day by day. From this, we can also see the understanding of family life among Soviet women in general.

Japanese women, although all those under the age of 40 have received a Western education, are all worthy of being called virtuous mothers and good wives. Although women's employment in Japan is much more developed than in our country, after their social service time is over, they return home to "manage household affairs," "raise children," and live a harmonious family life with their husbands.

The wife of President Roosevelt in the White House, during working hours, is an assistant to the President in handling government affairs; outside of working hours, she is the chief person responsible for the family, who declines all visits. From the President's health to the cleanliness of the house, she is responsible. It is said that when there is a banquet in the White House, the First Lady often goes to the kitchen to cook herself.

Therefore, I feel that modern women with knowledge should not consider themselves remarkable simply because they can serve society. To be a remarkable modern woman, one should also serve the family in addition to serving society.

In society, be a professional woman; in the family, be a virtuous mother and good wife. This is the modern standard woman.

American Women's "Difficulty in Choosing a Husband" 215

— Kang Tun

In the United States, although the number of boys and girls born is almost equal, women generally feel a fear of lacking "good husbands." It seems that there is a surplus of women. This phenomenon is certainly not biological.

In terms of general phenomena in world history, superior men are generally more numerous than women. And low-ability men, such as idiots, are also more numerous than men. These low-ability men are not physiologically incapable of marriage. However, they are generally abandoned by women and become single widowers.

The main reasons why there is a perceived lack of suitable men to be husbands are: first, the husband's talent must be higher than the wife's so as not to have the feeling of a phoenix following a crow; second, the wife's age must be younger than the husband's so that the husband leads and the wife follows; third, women who have received higher education have overly strict standards for choosing a partner, and the other party is likely to feel unworthy.

From these points of view, it is clear that women who have "difficulty in choosing a husband" in their hearts are mostly women who have received higher education. According to statistics from many universities and specialized schools, less than half and more than a quarter of female graduates remain single for life. These women who have received higher education feel the pain of lifelong loneliness; and society also invisibly loses so many virtuous wives and good mothers.

Nowadays, most women who have received a considerable education are prepared to dedicate themselves to society after graduation, but most women's occupations are nothing more than teachers, nannies, nurses, librarians, and so on. In these situations, unmarried men do not necessarily make up the majority. In addition, women like to be self-regarding and are unwilling to easily embark on a romantic path. And most men's choice of a partner does not necessarily welcome upright women. They use women's love of vanity to their advantage, some using seduction, and some simply amounting to abduction. The more self-regarding a woman is, the more difficult it is to get close to men.

Conversely, ordinary women's criteria for choosing a partner are naturally less demanding, and they may even lower their standards. The possibility of marriage is naturally greater. As for those women who have received higher education and harbor extravagant hopes, they initially raise their standards for choosing a partner too high. When their wishes are not fulfilled and they get older, they realize that youth does not wait for them, lower their standards, but the other party may not be willing to compromise because of the age difference.

The average age of marriage in the United States is 25 for men and 21 for women. Women who graduate from college are almost two or three years past the average marriage age. But men always choose women who are two or three years younger than themselves. Women in their mid-twenties can only marry men over 30. Moreover, women with higher ambitions always like to work for a few years after graduating from college, earning some income to prepare for marriage; or even pay off the debts they incurred while studying. Year after year, they delay, and the age standard for marriage becomes further and further away. According to statistics from Dr. Tamblin of Kyoto Life Insurance Company: women at the age of 20 have an average of two to three marriage opportunities within ten years. Women at the age of 30 have a half of a marriage opportunity within ten years. As a result, a large number of talented women remain single and lonely, embracing the bright moon for the rest of their lives!

In short, if a woman who has received a considerable education wants to enjoy a normal married life, she must be realistic and choose a partner at the right time before the age of 20, and never easily miss the precious time of youth.

An Interview with the Humorous Master Lin Yutang and His Wife (Part 2) 216

— Ji Ping

"Mr. Lin is a humorous writer, may I ask what criticisms you have of modern women?"

He thought for a moment, then smiled at his wife again, and the words came: "I think women who like to show off are bad! Generally, good women don't like to show off, they just raise children silently at home, fulfilling their great mission. Is being a new virtuous wife and good mother not a noble vocation? Because men cannot do the work of being a wife and mother at home, it can only be done by women. So a woman must be a virtuous wife and good mother, and a man must be a virtuous husband and good father." He paused for a while, and said again: "The women who show off the most in politics are the worst, but they are not enough to represent the new women." After he finished speaking, his wife expressed her opposition, saying, "You are going too far, no wonder the tabloids are spreading rumors about you." He said, "It's a fact, not an exaggeration."

"According to this, what should Mr. Lin's ideal new woman be like?"

He laughed, as if it were difficult to answer; after a while, he said eloquently: "This is too long to say, how can it be finished in a few words?"

"I have no choice but to combine a thousand sentences into one, please shorten it," I said.

"Okay! My ideal new woman, first of all, must be healthier than before; second, Chinese women are all dependent, lacking the independent spirit of Western women, which may be the result of social attitudes oppressing them. Chinese women are not as lively as Western women, but their quiet and peaceful attitude is better than theirs; future women should combine the two; third, sexual morality should be more liberated than it is now, I oppose men being able to liberate their sexual desires, being able to prostitute, being able to divorce and remarry, while women cannot be free. Some people say that liberating women's sexual morality will make social customs worse, which is a biased view, and it would be too cruel and unfair to place the responsibility for ruining social customs on women. In short, to liberate women, we must first correct social attitudes. The Hong Jian Yuan's remarriage caused a sensation in the whole society, and everyone attacked her, which led to her leaving the country. How can this be reasonable!

At this point, Mr. Lin's words came to an end. I talked to his wife for a long time. First I asked, "What attitude does Mrs. Lin take towards Mr. Lin?" "Both parties take a cooperative attitude. I am fully responsible for household affairs, and more important matters are discussed together and decided upon."

"Please tell us about your experience in managing a household."

"Household affairs are not about experience. I would like to talk about four points in a random way: First, I advocate open family finances. Large families often cheat on finances and accumulate private savings, which results in various tragedies; second, determine the budget and final accounts, and expenditures should not exceed the budget, so that household affairs will not be chaotic; third, cultivate children's automatic habits from an early age, do not rely on servants, and develop their common nature, do not use brute force; if children make mistakes, use appropriate methods to make them aware; do not often scold them, too much scolding will lose its effect; sometimes you can use other people's affairs to indirectly teach; fourth, children should be independent. My two thorns in the flesh studied in the United States and Germany for many years, and took care of cooking and laundry themselves. Although servants are now doing it for them, they must always take a supervisory attitude, because family hygiene is the most important thing for food, and if it is entrusted to others, it will not be reliable."

"What is your opinion on the new-style family?"

"I agree with the small family system, because it is economically independent, does not rely on others, does not shirk responsibility, can develop the ability of housewives, and there is no possibility of conflict between new and old opinions, which are unmatched by large families. However, it is one's duty to support one's parents, and one must not be negligent. I think that no matter how new or old, large or small the family is, housewives must not shirk their natural duty to take care of the family, must not have excessive entertainment; must not wear strange and gaudy clothes that do not fit their status; must not neglect the education of boys and girls; in addition to family affairs, must not forget the desire for knowledge and the public welfare of society."

"What kind of entertainment does madam do every day?" At this time, Mr. Lin put down his pen and snatched to say: "We walk in the suburbs every day, play with the children, don't often watch movies, occasionally go dancing, often attend friends' banquets, and there's nothing else."

Unintentionally, we talked for an hour and a half. Everyone is busy, so I had to say goodbye.

Corrigenda: In the previous issue, in the first line of this article, "On the eve of my visit," there is an extra word "we" under the word "I"; in the fifteenth line, "My government and people," the symbol "　" is wrongly printed as "etc."; in the twenty-third line, "Mrs. Lin interjected," interjected is wrongly written as "broadcast," especially corrected.

Beauty and Crime 217

— Hui Fang

In "Sexual Selection," the beautiful ones are the winners. In general, people have a love for beauty, and for ugly women, they feel disgust and displeasure. Therefore, people generally treat beauty with great tolerance and kindness, and treat ugly women with excessive coldness and meanness. No matter when or where, beautiful women are often welcomed by many opposite sexes and easily obtain sexual satisfaction, while ugly women are the opposite.

Precisely because beautiful women easily win the hearts of the opposite sex and receive generous treatment in society, it often causes them to fall into the dangers of daily life. Poisonous women and femme fatales mostly belong to beautiful women, which is very obvious. To investigate the reason, it can be analyzed into six points: First, people generally treat beautiful women with great forgiveness. Second, beautiful women are aware that they are "winners of sexuality," and tend to be negligent in daily life. Third, beautiful women easily obtain the love and hospitality of others, and easily develop various social relationships. Fourth, beautiful women are mostly slaves of vanity. Fifth, beautiful women easily provoke the temptation of the opposite sex and commit mistakes in terms of sex. Sixth, beautiful women waste more on decorations and clothing than ugly slaves.

Moreover, beautiful women often make men willing to be their protectors, and they are obedient to their orders. And the general public in society are mostly fooled by their beauty, mistakenly believing that such beautiful women would not commit terrible crimes.

The above are the reasons that make it easy for beautiful women to do wrong. Secondly, they often fall into great misfortune or commit great mistakes due to the opposite sex. Beautiful women are often the focus of attention of the opposite sex, causing many men who admire them to compete. Because of love disputes, on the one hand, they are suspected by women of the same sex, and on the other hand, they are jealous of the opposite sex, which is more intense than ordinary greed, and therefore the danger they are exposed to is even greater. There are very many tragedies of injury and murder that occur due to disputes between men and women.

Furthermore, men protecting beautiful women may be harmless in many places, but if a vicious man has a beautiful wife, he often uses her beauty to boast to the world, and thus indulges in his evil deeds. "Behind every great crime, there is a woman," this saying contains truth, meaning that women are directly or indirectly related to evil, especially saying that beautiful women easily make men commit greater crimes.

Snake (2) 221

— Qin Wang Yin Jiu

That day, no matter if it was spring or summer, there would always be such a day! The little mute, who was not afraid of anything, even Liu the madman, who was afraid of seeing people on the street, suddenly revealed an unexpected weakness in front of a tofu shop. He was first squatting on the street teasing a puppy, looking very happy, his bird-black face full of mischievous and lovely smiles; the corner of his clothes was completely covered in a pool of dirty water and he didn't even notice, his body was still bending backwards, his back almost touching the surface of the water, and the dog was lying on his chest. People who were used to seeing him like this were smiling at him, but unexpectedly, the child suddenly jumped up as if he had been electrocuted, let go of the dog, his face turned ashen, as if he had been greatly frightened, he held his head in his hands, and desperately jumped into the counter of the tofu shop, hiding behind a clerk, hugging the person's waist tightly, shaking all over; of course, everyone was alarmed by this!

"Hey! Why is this child so scared?"

Some people were asking each other; but the clerk in the tofu shop felt very sorry for him, and hurriedly turned around and comforted them:

"Don't panic! What did you see that made you so scared?"

"A snake! A snake!"

In this way, everyone knew that this mysterious wild child was so frightened because he saw a small snake.

The next day, he came to the market again. Some people deliberately wanted to test him. They first bought a three- or four-foot-long fire-red snake that had its teeth pulled out from a beggar, and deliberately threw it near him, while shouting:

"Oh dear! The snake is coming! The snake is coming!"

This time, the mute was even more frightened. He ran all the way back, crying so hard that he could hardly breathe; from that day on, he didn't dare to go out for a full month, and the errand of going to the street to buy things was once again taken over by his father! That officer of unknown name! took on the task of going.

The Construction of Cultural National Defense 232

— Meng Ruo

Recently, Japan has been paying great attention to the promotion of cultural diplomacy, spreading its culture overseas, which will be one of the important items of Japan's diplomatic policy this year. Foreign Minister Hirota strongly advocated this point in his diplomatic speech at the 68th resolution meeting. As a result of the agreement, it was decided to carry out various cultural activities with an international cultural undertaking fund of one million yuan, seeking cultural friendship and cooperation with countries around the world. This also shows Japan's ability to exert its diplomatic policies.

This makes us think of the necessity of building cultural national defense in our country. Our country's national crisis is getting heavier day by day, and all actions should be aimed at saving the nation and seeking survival. We not only need to have substantial preparations in the military field to make military national defense strong and solid, but also a revival in the cultural field. The revival of culture, imitating Japan's promotion of cultural diplomacy, we are afraid we have no time for this. However, it is a very urgent move to establish a strong cultural national defense domestically. Saving the country is the responsibility of the people of the whole country, and the cultural circles who have the responsibility of leading the society should stand in front and strive hard. This is the era task that people in cultural circles should fulfill.

To save today's dying China, comprehensively observing the public opinions expressed by all parties in the country, the only strategy is to launch a national liberation movement. The construction of cultural national defense should also follow this path. People generally engaged in cultural undertakings must do their utmost to advocate culturally, so that this movement can be realized as soon as possible. Not only to advocate, but also to guide. In our country's national liberation movement, the cultural circles should be the pioneer soldiers.

The resistance to the enemy on January 28 was the first sound of our country's national liberation movement. The student movements launched successively across the country after December 9 are an expansion of this movement. In the future, the responsibility of building cultural national defense can often be shouldered by this kind of movement.

However, how should the construction of cultural national defense be promoted? Regarding this point, it should be explained from all aspects. The education sector must change its education policy and implement education suitable for the national crisis. This matter is currently being researched by the Ministry of Education, and some educators are also enthusiastically discussing it, and there will definitely be considerable results in the future. The press must report accurate news and awaken the public with fair public opinion. Writers must use various methods to stimulate people's awareness of struggle. Other various cultural institutions should also do their part in their respective cultural fields. In short, striving to promote the national salvation movement culturally is the important task that the cultural circles should have in building cultural national defense in the future.

The Teahouse and Its Owner 233

— Family Member

In the afternoon, when the setting sun shone brightly on the storefront, the waiters began to get busy: carrying water, stoking the stove to make the fire blaze, and also moving tables and chairs. Li Sandie, the owner, sat by the counter, pointing with his mouth. While smoking his dry tobacco pipe. The attitude is calm and leisurely. He looks older than forty, slightly fat, his face is always blood red, and he is also energetic, so looking at him, he seems to be only nearly thirty years old. This is because the teahouse business is booming, and he has better days.

This teahouse is located in the most bustling section of the long street. Although the storefront is not very big, it does not feel crowded to place twenty or so square and round tables. It was opened in the generation of Li Sandie's father, and the days are extremely far away. This oldness lies in the signboard on the door, engraved with the two large convex characters "Jin Xing", because it has been a long time, it has been smoked black by the sunlight and vapor, and it is covered with dust, almost blurring and difficult to recognize what characters are on it.

After taking a full mouthful of smoke, he put away his dry tobacco pipe. After a while, he will be too busy to smoke. Then he will have to use his loud and respectful voice to greet every customer who comes in without stopping.

The first to arrive is always the old man Risheng Bo, with white hair and a thick mustache, the oldest customer in the teahouse. He comes every day and occupies a certain seat. Therefore, almost everyone knows him. He likes to provoke idleness. When he opens his mouth, he is often nagging endlessly. It can be said that he is too verbose, but he is old and has a gentle temperament, so no one dislikes him. Sometimes he also becomes the most popular temporary storyteller in the teahouse.

He walks very slowly. When he comes, he first walks to the counter and nods to the owner, Li Sandie. Then he takes out a dry tobacco pipe from the pocket of his half-new long gown and walks to a recognized table next to him, lights a paper roll, and slowly smokes while talking to the owner.

Before long, the teahouse is filled with tea drinkers, and there are no empty seats left.

Some of these people are regular customers, some are occasional travelers who use it as a place to rest their feet, and some are from nearby villages who have finished their work and come to the market to relieve their boredom.

In short, every afternoon, the Jin Xing Teahouse is bustling with an endless stream of footprints until it gradually becomes quiet in the evening.

With so many people, the sound is unusually noisy, and it is almost impossible to hear clearly when speaking face to face. You have to raise your voice, so the air becomes more tense and turbulent. Everyone seems to have a heart that needs to be fully opened and speak freely when they come here. Everyone is so energetic and happy.

Smoke and water vapor fill the surroundings, causing some people to cough and some people's eyes to tear. The waiter is too busy to handle it. This person wants water, and that person wants something. He is still overwhelmed, so this person shouts faster, and that person also shouts faster. At this time, Li, the owner, sits on the counter with an indescribable triumphant expression and has to come down to help.

Risheng Bo smoked his dry tobacco pipe, watched Li Sandie walk closer, and smiled enviously, revealing his yellow teeth:

——Haha! Sandie, business is really good!

Sandie is not only the first to come but also the last to leave. When he leaves, the teahouse is occupied by a silence. The ground is littered with melon seed shells and peanut skins.

The waiter is cleaning up, and Li Sandie is clearing up the accounts. Just that bamboo tube, which is more than five feet high and has a bowl-sized opening, is filled with copper coins to the opening, which is enough to make him indescribably happy and happily drink more white rose wine in the evening.

It is something that no one can imagine to support a family of seven or eight people and still have a surplus by relying on a teahouse with a hollow facade. The people in the village are all envious.

After a lot of days, the situation gradually changed.

In the afternoon, the sun is still the same sun as before, and it still shines on the facade of Jin Xing Teahouse as usual, and Li Sandie also sits in the counter as usual, but he smiles less and frowns more. The customers are getting deserted day by day. At first, he thought the price was too high, so he tried his best to lower it, but the result was that fewer and fewer people drank tea, and the business got worse step by step. So he fired the waiters and only kept an apprentice and himself, but there were only a few people scattered and doing nothing all day long, and they were bored.

As for Risheng Bo, he still comes every day as an exception. And people who were like Risheng Bo some time ago have not been seen for a long time. Seeing that scene and thinking of the past situation, Risheng Bo would sigh and say:

——The year is not good, the days are hard, and even the money for a few cups of tea has to be saved.

The listener, Li Sandie, had nothing to answer, but returned a bitter and resentful look.

Like other shops on the street, the once prosperous Jin Xing Teahouse has gradually declined since then.

Their Home 234

— Liang Qiyun

Home, home, sweet home.

There is no place more lovely than home,

There is no place more lovely than home. — Ballad.

The dim sky was taut with a cheerless face. And it began to cry again. Tears hung down in rows. — At this time, it was raining.

Two young lads turned into that small tavern together. They sat down in the corner. …

The waiter brought up the plates, and the plates seemed to be steaming. As they picked up their chopsticks, snow also fell mixed in with the rain. Like falling flowers falling from the sky.

The one who put down his chopsticks first looked out the window and said with a sense of feeling,

"Look, it's snowing."

The other one replied.

"I'm really afraid. Every time I see snow, I think of home. — The snow in my hometown is more flavorful. This place is no good, nothing is good. Only people's hearts are much colder than ours."

The one who spoke first was tall, with messy hair, and a pale face with a hint of melancholy. He looked up, and then said,

"Yes, I don't understand why some people here always live such a dull life. —"

"Otherwise, what do you want them to do!"

"Is that all there is to it?" The tall man confronted the other with this question angrily. The man shook his stout body.

"But, what can they do?"

The tall man seemed to be moved by these words and fell silent.

The wind blew a few snowflakes in. On the floor near the shop entrance, there were a few more drops of water. People's feet trampled on it, making it look even more damp and dirty. — The snow here is never as great as in the north. The snow in the south is really an imbecile.

The stout one raised his voice again to break the silence:

"At first, when I first came here, it was okay. In the newspapers, I read with tears in my eyes. On the streets, I ran blindly with the marching crowd. —

"Once, the crowd was clamoring on the street, a large crowd of people of all kinds. A raspy voice shouted enthusiastically, "Welcome the public to participate!" Often, I was full of thoughts…"

He paused slightly. Again,

"That was so good. I squeezed into the crowd and walked along. It was as if I was walking on the official road in my hometown. … I saw a small Western-style building and thought it was my family's tiled house… We walked a lot of roads together, and later I didn't know what road we were on, and the crowd dispersed there. I ran with a hot heart

Page 22

Back to the apartment, lying on the bed, always thinking of home, unable to sleep, and kept having insomnia until dawn."

"—"

The tall man did not speak, but his pale face revealed a look of surprise.

The fat man began to sob again.

"Now, you see, the home is gone, where is the second home?…"

Sighing, sadly.

Thinking of home, there are too many beautiful things in my hometown… snow-covered mountain peaks, frozen rivers… thinking like this, two pairs of tired eyes froze…

Quietly silent. Silence spread like smoke again.

It was getting dark. Dusk walked in softly. He covered the sky with his big hands. He was jealous of the day, so he had such a job. However, this was also in vain for him. — The night was about to follow, and soon he would be swallowed up by others.

Outside —

Still, the rain chases the snow, and the snow chases the rain.

Moreover, there is also a bit of wind. — Close your eyes and quietly, you can hear the wind sobbing in the sound of rain and snow dripping.

Loneliness 235

— Zhiyuan

Loneliness, irresistible loneliness, washes over me like a flood.

In this room of mine, there is no animal life other than myself, only the life of a few plants: two pots of maidenhair fern hanging under the beam, two pots of asparagus fern, one of which has little hope of survival, and one pot of plum with withered flowers from last winter, sprouting a few tender greens. I have infinite affection and love for the companions of life in this room. Every night I can forget what the doctor told me I should do, but I never forget the two pots of clear water that these two pots of maidenhair fern deserve. They feel comfortable and at ease in this room of mine, I think. They sprout tender shoots, gradually drooping their green stems, almost reaching the bottom layer of the bookshelf. And surprisingly, they actually bloom with white three-petaled small flowers. So white, so small, hiding behind the dense green leaves, even I didn't notice. When I saw them, several flowers had already withered lonely, such a lonely self-opening and self-falling, which moved me greatly. For the asparagus fern, I also have the greatest expectation and care to serve. I heard that it wants to drink milk, so I asked the neighbor to wash a little water from the empty milk bottle to irrigate it. In this way, I saved a dying Western strain. There are new buds. One morning I found that a pot on this desk had a half-inch of green, pale white new branches; I was surprised by this news of life. This new bud grows unusually fast. I took a joint of an old branch next to it as a size. Every night I can see this soft and plump branch tip, slightly curved towards the sun, pointing to a higher joint of the old branch next to it. Two days later, another new bud broke out of the soil layer, extending its life to the sun in the same posture and speed.

I thought, if I were imprisoned in a prison at this moment, and there was only one person, as long as there was such a little green life accompanying me, as long as I could use the raw materials of my own life to complete another life, I would be joyful, happy and dancing.

My situation is much better than being imprisoned in a prison, and there is already green life accompanying me. But I am lonely. Irresistible emptiness washes over me like a flood.

In the morning, the orange-yellow sun shines on my eyelids, giving me the sour feeling of squeezing the juice from the orange peel and shooting it on my eyelids when I was playing as a child. The color of the morning glow is unpredictably rapid: orange-yellow instantly becomes golden, followed by a string of pigeon bells with a metallic sound. From the rise and fall of the bell sound, I can imagine the dance of the pigeons carrying the golden early sun on my roof, linking together to form a pagoda. The bell sound is faster, I know that they have completed the spire and ascended to the higher distant sky, leaving her at the bottom to indulge my fantasy. So I lotusly sat up: isn't the pagoda also a kind of tomb?

But even the tomb is empty, lonely.

Storytelling in Song Form 236

Xu Wenbi's Opening Chapter

City Sounds (1340) 10:00 AM to 11:00 AM

Opening: "Traveling in the Rain"

Dark: Dark clouds fill the sky. Heavy, heavy, heavy rain falls incessantly. Fine, fine, fine rain never stops. Muddy, muddy, muddy, the road is hard to walk. Wind: Sharp, sharp wind assaults the face. Wet, wet, wet soaks the traveler's clothes. Road long, long, long, a thousand miles to traverse. Going, going, going, the journey is difficult. Tears: Tears flow unceasingly. Steps falter, falter, falter, weary feet are exhausted. I resent, resent, resent my family's decline. Anxious, anxious, anxious, each day feels like a year. Helpless, helpless, helpless, yet I must visit my relatives. Parting, parting, parting, leaving my home. Expenses exhausted. Belly empty. Eyes dizzy. Limping, limping. I fear this journey may prevent me from seeing my mother again. I ponder, ponder, ponder, as the sun threatens to set. He is, heartbroken. Gut wrenched. Steps falter, eyes blur. The road slippery, slippery, slippery, the mud engulfs my legs. Strength failing, failing, I collapse in the mud. Breath faint, faint, faint, only a breath remains. Rain pouring, pouring, the rain is even heavier than before. In a hazy dream, my soul returns to my hometown.

Lu Qiuxia's Double Pearl Phoenix

China and West (1040) 7:00 PM to 8:00 PM

Opening: "Bao Yu Cries for Qing Wen"

The best among the maids in the Grand View Garden. Jade shattered, fragrance extinguished, buried beneath the earth. The sentimental young master wails loudly. His heart filled with complaints, all thoughts turned to ashes. Ignorant little maids speak carelessly. They say she, played in the human world for twenty-eight years. A jade maiden descended from the ninth heaven. I cry for you, tranquil, dignified, and virtuous. Suited for anger and laughter, you pleased my heart. I cry for you, intelligent beyond compare, with a clever mind. Extraordinary talent, a great intellect. I cry for you, with a righteous heart, capable like a man. A pure and innocent nature, like a child. Qing Wen ah, which of the four beauties can compare to you? The best of women, ancient and modern. We were together, morning and night, for a few years. Guarding and mending the impure jade, attended by a fairy maiden. Qing Wen ah, sometimes reading aloud on cold winter days. Only you, kept me company all night, unafraid of the cold. Qing Wen ah, sewing the fur coat while sick, your affection was deep. Every stitch, every thread, pleasing to the eye. Qing Wen ah, that old woman Wang deserves to be killed. Spreading rumors, daring to slander. Qing Wen ah, the mistress believed the gossip. Cooking the crane, burning the zither, forcing you to return. I watched silently, not speaking out. It's just like, forcing Yang Guifei to her death at Mawei. Qing Wen ah, you begged in vain, leaving in sorrow. Saying, how could beautiful features be a source of disaster. Qing Wen ah, you returned to your immortal ranks, wronged and full of grievance. Still doing, making a joyful flower goddess, returning the flawless jade. Qing Wen ah, the courtyard is desolate and cold, unnoticed by others. Only I, the master of the Yi Hong Courtyard, know the sorrow. After crying, I burn paper offerings. The dark wind is bleak, the night drawing to a close. My hair stands on end as I quietly return.
